Organizational Rules

"Organizational Rules of the Shanghai National Contribution One-Day Income Movement Promotion Committee": Article 1: This association is named the Shanghai National Contribution One-Day Income Movement Promotion Committee. Article 2: The purpose of this association is to handle the national one-day income contribution to the country to enrich national defense. Article 3: This association is organized by the following agencies and groups: (1) Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department; (2) Shanghai Municipal Government; (3) Garrison Headquarters; (4) Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau; (5) Shanghai Municipal Farmers' Association; (6) Shanghai Municipal General Labor Union; (7) Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce; (8) Shanghai Municipal Education Association; (9) Shanghai Municipal Lawyers' Association; (10) Shanghai Municipal Certified Public Accountants Association; (11) Shanghai Municipal Physicians' Association; (12) Shanghai Municipal National Medical Association; (13) Shanghai Municipal Banking Association; (14) Shanghai Municipal Money Industry Association; (15) Shanghai Municipal Daily Newspaper Association; (16) Shanghai Municipal Journalists' Association; (17) First Special District Citizens' Federation; (18) Second Special District Citizens' Federation; (19) Shanghai Municipal Local Association; (20) China Cultural Construction Association; (21) Federation of Universities; (22) Secondary School Advancement Association; (23) Shanghai Branch of the China Aviation Construction Association; and other groups approved by this meeting. Article 4: This association establishes five standing committee members, who are recommended by the committee to preside over daily affairs. Article 5: This association establishes three departments: General Affairs, Donation Affairs, and Official Propaganda, each with a principal and deputy director, who are recommended by the committee. Article 6: The responsibilities of the General Affairs Department are as follows: (1) Handling the association's documents; (2) Handling the association's accounting matters; (3) Other matters of public relations and contact. Article 7: The responsibilities of the Donation Affairs Department are as follows: (1) Soliciting donations; (2) Collecting and delivering donations; (3) Reporting and reviewing donations. Article 8: The responsibilities of the Propaganda Department are as follows: (1) Planning various propaganda matters; (2) Handling various official propaganda matters. Article 9: This association establishes a Donation Custody Committee, which is organized by seven members mutually recommended by the committee, to be solely responsible for the custody of donations. Article 10: The donations received by this association, unless otherwise specified by the donors, will be remitted to the central government for the purpose of enriching national defense. Article 11: The donations received by this association from all walks of life will be disclosed in the newspaper every day and reported in total once a month to show credibility. Article 12: This association establishes a general manager, who assists in all association affairs in accordance with the instructions of the standing committee members. Article 13: This association may, depending on the complexity of the association's affairs, transfer several staff members from participating agencies and groups to handle the affairs, without additional salary. Article 14: The expenses of this association shall be jointly raised by participating agencies and groups, and donations shall not be misappropriated. Article 15: This association holds a regular meeting once every half month. When necessary, the standing committee members may convene a temporary meeting. Article 16: These rules may be amended at any time if there are any omissions. Article 17: These rules shall be implemented after being passed by the committee meeting.

Shanghai County Government Proclamation: Land Price Tax Collection, Hoping that the Public Will Actively Pay

The land price tax of Shanghai County was officially collected the day before yesterday (the 20th). In addition to issuing a proclamation, the Shanghai County Government also convened the district chiefs of each district to give instructions, urging them to instruct the township chiefs to notify each business owner to pay on time. The original text of the proclamation is recorded as follows: It is hereby announced that the field tax of this county has been ordered to be changed to the land price tax this year. During the tenure of the previous County Magistrate Ye, preparations were started. At the beginning of the tenure of this County Magistrate, successive reports were received from local associations and local people, with many suggestions regarding the estimated land price and the tax rate set in this county. It was considered that the implementation of this new policy was a major event concerning the land policy formulated by the late Premier Sun Yat-sen. If it is not handled carefully from the beginning, it will be difficult to achieve complete benefits. The local association suggested that, on the premise of not hindering the provincial and county budgets and not increasing the burden on farmers, land price tax for the first period should be collected while representatives (ten people) should be recommended to properly evaluate the land price and tax rate in the city, so that the tax payments can be corrected during the second period of collection, so as to facilitate both officials and the people. The report was considered feasible and was approved. In addition, a sample of the land price tax license was drafted and submitted for approval. Now, Instruction No. 30419 from the Department of Finance has been received, which modifies and issues the sample of the land price tax license, and stipulates the collection period, land price tax rate, and self-sealing of bids and submission to the counter, penalties for late payments, etc., ordering immediate compliance and reporting. Compliance is required, and it is now decided to start collecting the first period of land price tax for this year on November 20th of this year. In addition to the notification and the report, this proclamation is hereby issued to all business owners in this county to comply with it in its entirety. Please pay the amount of silver due as stated on the notification form to the counter within the specified time limit and obtain a license to secure your property. It should be noted that the starting date for the collection of this year's new policy of field tax is later than the established precedents and the stipulated time limit, which is already considered too late. Now is the time when the autumn harvest is abundant and the financial situation is ample. You must seize this opportunity to comply with the requirements and actively pay the tax. Those who still fail to pay at the counter will be summoned and pursued, and a fine of 5% per annum will be levied in accordance with the provisions of Chapter 8 of Part 4 of the Land Law. Do not wait and see and make mistakes, which may lead to penalties. This is a warning.

The Municipal Government Regulates Food Prices and Stabilizes Grain Prices, Organizes Grain Transit Registration, and All Transit to Other Ports Must Be Transported with a Registration Certificate, and the Two Railway Bureaus and Customs Have Been Ordered to Comply and Assist

According to a report from the Social Affairs Bureau to the Shanghai Municipal Government, in order to regulate food prices and stabilize grain prices, the government has specially organized grain transit registration and transferred it to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Railways to order the Customs and Railway Bureau to comply and assist. The details are recorded as follows:

Document from the Social Affairs Bureau to the Municipal Government

The Social Affairs Bureau reported to the Municipal Government that, in order to regulate food prices and stabilize grain prices, it is first necessary to understand the status of surplus and deficiency and to handle it with accuracy. The investigation of rice and grain sales in this city has been carried out by this bureau for many years. However, the quantity of transit grain is only compiled statistically based on the customs reports on a monthly basis. In the period of stable market prices, it is sufficient for reference. However, once a food crisis occurs, it is impossible to understand the true situation, and it is difficult to control it temporarily. For example, the recent soaring prices of rice, wheat, and flour in this city were caused by many factors. However, according to the investigation, the impact of a large amount of transit is not insignificant. After weighing the market situation and consulting with seed merchants, this bureau believes that if the quantity of rice, wheat, flour, and beans in transit in this city is not checked at ordinary times, it will not be easy to adjust it temporarily. In order to prevent and maintain it in advance, organizing transit registration is an effective method. However, the matter must be assisted by the Customs and the Railway Bureau before it can be implemented. Therefore, the "Shanghai Rice, Wheat, Flour, and Beans Transit Registration Measures" and the application form, certificate, and registration certificate are prepared and submitted to you for review. Please consult the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Railways to transfer them to the Customs and the Railway Bureau to comply and assist, and send a copy to the Ministry of Interior for verification. It is really a public service.

Grain Transit Registration Measures

Shanghai Rice, Wheat, Flour, and Beans Transit Registration Measures: (1) Anyone who purchases rice, wheat, flour, and beans in this city for transit to other ports must apply for registration at the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and hold a registration certificate before they can be transported. (2) The application form in the preceding paragraph shall be prepared and issued by the Social Affairs Bureau. All transit merchants or merchants may directly request it from the Food Section of the Fourth Division of the Bureau. (3) The application form must state the following: 1. Name, place of origin, occupation, and address of the applicant; 2. Goods and grades; 3. Place of origin, price, and quantity; 4. Name of the selling merchant and name of the manager; 5. Date of loading and name of the ship or train number; 6. Delivery address; 7. Name of the receiving merchant and name of the manager. It must also be certified by the relevant grain industry association in this city. The grain industry association mentioned in the preceding paragraph refers to the Bean Rice Industry Association, the Rice Number Industry Association, the Rice Milling Industry Association, and the Rice Grain Industry Association for Resale for rice; the Miscellaneous Grain Oilcake Industry Association for wheat; the Flour Mill Industry Association for flour; the Bean Rice Industry Association, the Miscellaneous Grain Oilcake Industry Association, and the Miscellaneous Grain Retail Industry Association for beans. (4) After receiving the application form and certificate from the applicant, if the Social Affairs Bureau considers the report to be true, it shall immediately issue a transit registration certificate. 5. The application certificate paper and transit registration certificate in the preceding paragraph shall be issued by the Social Affairs Bureau without any fees. 6. In case of food shortage in this city, the Social Affairs Bureau may temporarily suspend transit registration or reduce the quantity of transit. 7. Rice, wheat, flour, and beans that have not been approved for registration shall absolutely not be allowed to be transported. 8. These measures shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Municipal Government.

Customs and Railway Bureau Ordered to Comply

The Municipal Government has transferred it to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Railways to transfer it to the Customs and the Railway Bureau to comply and assist. Now, the Jianghai Customs and the Two Railway Bureaus have received the order from the Ministry. The order No. 4263 from the Ministry of Railways is recorded as follows: "Approved Shanghai Municipal Government's Consultation No. 5573 of October 31 of this year, which opened, 'According to the report of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, (omitted in the middle) etc., attached are the registration measures and other documents. According to this, the proposed Shanghai Rice, Wheat, Flour, and Beans Transit Registration Measures are for the purpose of regulating food prices and preventing smuggling abroad, which is a necessary plan. In addition to submitting it to the Executive Yuan for review and consultation, the registration measures are hereby copied and sent to you. It is hoped that you will take note of this and quickly transfer it to the Railway Bureau for assistance and reply. ' etc. Approval is hereby granted, and assistance should be provided. Hereafter, if any stations in Shanghai report the transportation of rice, wheat, flour, and beans for transit to other ports, it shall be limited to those holding a registration certificate from the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, otherwise, the railway shall refuse to load it to assist. In addition to replying, the registration measures are copied and issued for your compliance. '"

Sun Ke Speaks Freely About His Feelings on the Trip South, Praising the Organization of Guangxi Province, But the Financial System Still Needs to Be Sorted Out, Guangdong Province Has Made Progress in All Aspects, and Society Is More Stable Than Before

According to the Central News Agency, Sun Ke, the Speaker of the Legislative Yuan, was dispatched by the Central Government on the 21st of last month, accompanied by Legislative Yuan members Li Wenfan, Liang Hancao, Fu Bingchang, Xie Baoqiao, and others, to go south to attend the state funeral of the late Chairman Hu. After that, they went to Guangxi, Hunan, and other places to visit scenic spots. They returned to Nanjing tired of traveling at noon on the 20th. On the same day, they took a plane to this city from Nanjing with Deng Gang, the director of the Guangdong Pacification Commissioner's Office in Nanjing. At 10:00 AM on the 21st, they met with newspaper reporters at their private residence on Columbia Road to talk freely about their trip south.

Bai Will Go North

According to Sun, after attending Mr. Hu's state funeral, he took a detour to Guangxi, Hunan, and other provinces to travel. He stayed in Guilin for four days and visited Li Zongren, Bai Chongxi, and others. The date of Bai's entry into Nanjing has not yet been decided. After the major demobilization affairs in Guangxi Province are completely completed, he can go north. In short, Bai's entry into Nanjing is only a matter of time. The number of people mobilized in Guangxi Province this time has reached more than 300,000, so it takes a lot of time to handle the demobilization.

Characteristics of Guangxi Province

Sun expressed his appreciation for the local organization in Guangxi Province and said that it can be called a model province in China and can be used as a reference for the whole country. The most obvious characteristic of the organization is the militia. The militia organization consists of ten households as one Jia and one hundred and sixty households as one village. Above the village is the township, and above the township is the county. The whole province has telephone access in all directions. The provincial government can notify all counties, townships, and villages in the province by telephone within two hours. Education in the whole province has also made progress. Each village has at least one elementary school. The principal is concurrently the village chief. At the same time, the village chief is also the commander of the militia. There are a total of more than 20,000 villages in the whole province. As for the financial system of Guangxi Province, the currency in circulation on the market is still the Guangxi currency. Compared with the legal tender, a premium must be added, ranging from 5% to 7%. Therefore, the financial system still needs to be sorted out.

Progress in Guangdong Affairs

Sun continued to say that since the establishment of the Guangdong government, the province's military, civil administration, finance, etc. have made obvious progress compared with the past. As for the social situation in Guangdong Province, it is also more stable than before. Although prices are higher than before, the export of goods is increasing day by day. In short, hundreds of undertakings in Guangdong Province are making efforts to promote them, and I think there will be obvious progress again soon.

Suiyuan Incident

Sun believes that the banditry in Suiyuan will eventually be eliminated in the short term. Regarding the German-Japanese alliance, which is widely rumored in the market, Sun only said that the theory of the German-Japanese alliance cannot be determined to be impossible at present. Once it becomes a reality as rumored, it is dared to predict that the relationship between Britain, France, and the United States will become more and more close.

Yesterday, the Banking Industry and Money Industry Held a Joint Meeting to Jointly Study the Income Tax, and It Was Decided to Collect, Classify, and Summarize the Opinions of All Parties, and Then Hold a Meeting to Approve and Submit Them to the Ministry for Contribution and Adoption

The Income Tax Subcommittee of the Shanghai Banking Association and the Income Tax Research Committee of the Money Industry Association held a joint meeting at the Hong Kong Road Banking Club at 4:00 PM yesterday. The committee members of the Banking Subcommittee were Cai Chengxin of China, Feng Zhiwu of Jiaotong, Zhang Gongyun of Shanghai, He Xueyu of Jincheng, Yao Yinpeng of Zhonghui, Wang Xinggeng of Zhejiang Xingye, Li Suran of Salt Industry, Yuan Youcheng of Dalu, Yao Qiying of Kenye, Li Jianchi of Zhongnan, Zhang Jinglu of Guohua, Shen Bolong of Guohuo, Hu Xi'an of Siming, Yang Shandeng of China Agriculture and Industry, Qin Shuxin of Four Banks Savings Association, and the committee members of the Money Industry Committee were Zhuang Yunqing of Tongrun Money Shop and Feng Yigui of Fuyuan Money Shop. The secretary-general of the Banking Association, Lin Kang, attended. Cai Chengxin presided over the meeting, and Gu Yan recorded the minutes. First, the chairman reported that although the Ministry of Finance had approved the extension of the interest income tax on deposits to New Year's Day next year, it will be soon. Although banking associations, banking associations, banks, and money shops in various places have put forward opinions, how should they be collected and merged? The opinions will be submitted to the Ministry for contribution, hoping to be adopted. Then, the study began. The opinions on income tax from banking associations, banking associations, member banks, money industry associations, and member money shops in various places were collected, merged, and classified, and it was resolved that the classification would be completed quickly, mimeographed, and then submitted to the next decision-making meeting for approval before submitting it to the Ministry of Finance for contribution of opinions. The meeting adjourned at about 6:00 PM.

The Labor Dispute at the Husi Jinghua Yarn Factory is Expected to Be Resolved, the Situation of Xihua Resuming Work and the Internal and External Cotton Situation Has Also Eased, The Labor Dispute in Hudong Has Disappeared, and the Current Situation of Rihua is Quiet, and the Workers' Representatives of Each Factory Held Another Meeting Yesterday Morning

According to Dagong News Agency, the workers of the Japanese-owned Xihua First, Second, and Third Factories on Laobeisheng Road in Husi resumed work yesterday. The Toyota Yarn Factory on Zhongshan Road is sorting out its internal affairs and is scheduled to start work next Monday. The Rihua Caojiadu Factory is heavily guarded to prevent labor disputes from occurring. The details of each situation are recorded as follows:

Xihua Resumed Work Yesterday Morning

After the joint strike of all the workers of the Xihua First, Second, and Third Factories on Laobeisheng Road on the evening of the 19th, the representatives of the workers (18 people) went to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau in the morning of the 20th to petition, requesting a quick relief. At 4:00 PM, the factory informed the workers through the heads of various departments and classes that the factory would agree to increase wages in the same way as other factories, hoping that the workers would work with peace of mind. Therefore, most of the workers agreed, and 70% to 80% of the workers who worked day and night have entered the factory to work. It is expected that all the workers will enter the factory to work this morning.

Toyota Will Start Work on Monday

Five days have passed since the general strike of the workers of the Toyota First and Second Factories on Zhongshan Road Bridge. After the chairman of the local association of this city, Du Yuesheng, and the director of the Sino-Japanese Trade Association, Qian Xinzhi, visited Ritsuichiro Funatsu, the chairman of the Japanese Textile Industry Association in China, and jointly invited the labor and management to mediate, the factory expressed its acceptance of the workers' demands, and the workers also made concessions on some of the terms. All the workers are scheduled to resume work tomorrow morning. The various items destroyed in the second factory have already been sorted out and are being prepared to start work next Monday. However, the Japanese Marine Corps soldiers and armored vehicles stationed inside and outside the factory have not been withdrawn, and Chinese patrol police are also stationed along the road outside the factory.

General Situation of Each Factory

All the workers of the Interior and Exterior Cotton First Factory on Xiaoshadu Laobeisheng Road are still on strike. Only more than 200 people in the weaving department of the Second Factory are working. Less than 40% of the workers in the Fifth, Sixth, Seventh, and Third Factories on West Suzhou Road are working. All the workers in the Eighth Factory on Gordon Road are on strike. It is estimated that 60% to 70% of the workers in the Ninth Factory on Maigen Road have entered the factory. Because the workers of each factory have not fully resumed work, it is difficult to work, and work is sometimes suspended, and the production rate has been greatly reduced. In addition, the factory of the Japanese-owned Rihua Yarn Factory in Caojiadu on Laobeisheng Road is scheduled to pay the wages for the previous period yesterday. However, because it is rumored outside that the workers will also join the strike after the factory pays the wages, the factory specially requested the headquarters of the Japanese Marine Corps to send more than 30 armed Marine Corps soldiers to stay in the factory for precautionary purposes. Outside the factory, an armored gun vehicle No. 26 was also parked, and Tan Baoshou, the director of the Caojiadu Branch of the Public Security Bureau, also personally led more than 20 police officers to be stationed inside and outside the factory to protect it. There has been no labor dispute. As for other factories such as the Tongxing First and the Gongda Third Factories, they are all working as usual.

Workers' Meetings at Various Factories

More than 300 workers from the striking yarn factories in the Husi District intended to hold a meeting of representatives from various factories in the Pingmin New Village on Zhongshan Road at about 10:00 AM yesterday. After hearing the news, the Xinzao Branch of the district immediately sent police to suppress and disperse them. Then the workers of each factory gathered again in an empty house in a remote area of Danzi Bay to hold a meeting. The Caojiadu Branch also tried to persuade them to disperse, and no incident occurred.

Hudong Pudong is Quiet

In addition to the fact that most of the workers of the Shanghai Second and Third Factories at the Guangxin Wharf in Yangshupu, Hudong, have resumed work, the labor disputes in various factories such as the Tongxing Second, Dakang, Gongda Second, Yufeng One, Two, and Donghua have been eliminated. All the workers of the Rihua Yarn Factory in Lujiazui, Pudong, are working as usual, and the situation is extremely peaceful.

The Shanghai Branch of Guangdong Bank Extends the Resumption of Business

After Guangdong Bank suspended business on September 4 last year, it successfully planned to resume business with the assistance of Song Ziwen, the chairman of the Bank of China. The share capital is about 8 million yuan, including 2 million yuan of Class A preferred shares, 4.5 million yuan of Class B preferred shares, and 1.5 million yuan converted from old shares. The chairman is Song Ziwen, and the directors are Sun Ke, Wu Tiecheng, Deng Mianren, Huo Dingcun, Hu Yun, Song Zian, Li Fuhou, Tang Haian, Gen Fuyun, Huo Zhitin, Guo Shun, Feng Gengguang, Jiang Xiao, Pin, Huo Baoshu, Lao Jingxiu, Lin Bingyan, Li Shufen, Li Bingchao, Chen Jianpo, Guo Xing, and Bai Qinghai. Now the Hong Kong head office has decided to resume business tomorrow. As for the resumption date of the branches in San Francisco, Taishan, Siam, Hankou, and Shanghai, it remains to be decided by the head office. As for the manager of the Shanghai branch, Zhang Yingpu has been appointed. It was originally scheduled to resume business at the same time on the 23rd, but a telegram has been sent to the head office to resume business after the head office resumes business. The date has not been decided. It is said that it will be opened after Chairman Song Buwen returns to Shanghai from Hong Kong.

Wan Province Hexian Detains Rice; Grain Traders Urge Release; Jiashang and Other Counties in Zhejiang Province Continue to Obstruct Grain Transport; Petition to the Ministry of Railways for Swift Allocation of Grain Transport Vehicles

Regarding the procedures for Shanghai grain merchants purchasing rice and grain from Zhejiang province, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce issues certificates for passage. However, Jiashang and other counties are still obstructing the process, causing inconvenience to transportation. Simultaneously, Hexian in Anhui province has also detained over a hundred rice boats. The Shanghai Grain and Oilcake Traders Association, to maintain the food supply for Shanghai citizens, has again requested the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to telegraph both Zhejiang and Anhui provinces for facilitation, and has petitioned the Ministry of Railways for a swift allocation of grain transport vehicles for regulation. The details of each situation are recorded below:

Letter to the Chamber of Commerce I

Respected Sirs, the circulation of domestic rice and grains has long been implemented by order of the Central Government. We have received reports from our colleagues at Xie Changde and others that rice and grains purchased from Anhui province and transported to Hexian were suddenly seized, and the people detained. Other rice boats, more than a hundred in total, were also detained simultaneously, and falsely reported to the provincial government as aiding the enemy. Such self-governance by the county is truly detrimental to the people's food supply. We request that you forward our plea to your esteemed association and urgently telegraph the Anhui Provincial Government to strictly prohibit such behavior. Anhui province is a rich rice-producing area, and has historically supplied surplus grain to other areas with large populations. This time, Hexian has detained more than a hundred rice boats, and has even accused them of aiding the enemy based on unfounded speculation, acting arbitrarily and clearly violating government orders. At this time of peak sales of new grains, suddenly blocking the outflow is no different from adding shackles to Anhui farmers. Furthermore, Shanghai relies on neighboring provinces for its food supply, which will cause extreme panic. Our association, mindful of this, is deeply concerned. Therefore, we are forwarding this information to you and request that your esteemed association promptly petition the Anhui Provincial Government to strictly order Hexian to immediately release all detained grain boats, and to issue an order to all subordinate counties that they must not deliberately obstruct grain transport in the future, in accordance with the Central Government's intention to circulate domestic rice and grain. This is our earnest prayer.

Letter to the Chamber of Commerce II

Respected Sirs, regarding the ban on grain exports from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, our association previously sent a letter requesting your esteemed association to telegraph the governments of both provinces, requesting the lifting of the ban. We received a reply from the Zhejiang Provincial Government, a telegram from Chairman Huang, stating that surplus grain for transport must be formally certified by your association, and transportation permits must be obtained at the place of purchase and transport, in accordance with the province's food import and export registration regulations, to prevent smuggling, etc. A copy of the Zhejiang Provincial Food Import and Export Registration Regulations was also enclosed. Previously, our association received a copy of Chairman Huang's reply from the local association of this city, and immediately agreed with your esteemed association to handle the certification procedures. Meanwhile, we requested the local association to petition the Zhejiang Provincial Government to order all subordinate counties to facilitate the purchase and transport of food by Shanghai grain merchants, based on the certification documents from your esteemed association, without any obstruction. Currently, our colleagues purchasing food from Zhejiang province all report to our association for verification and then request your esteemed association to issue certificates, which are then presented to the local grain merchants at the place of purchase, who then directly submit them to the local county or city government for the issuance of transportation permits. This is in full compliance with Articles 3 and 4 of the Zhejiang Provincial Food Import and Export Registration Regulations, which have already been implemented. However, our colleagues have repeatedly reported that Jiashing, Leqing, Pingyang, Linhai, Huangyan, Wenling and other counties claim that they have not received provincial orders and refuse to allow the transport of food awaiting transport that holds certificates from your esteemed association. Such obstruction is burdensome for merchants. We are again writing to earnestly request your esteemed association to urgently telegraph the Zhejiang Provincial Government to order Jiashing and other counties to comply with the provisions of Article 3 of the registration regulations and promptly issue transportation permits for food awaiting transport that holds certificates from your esteemed association, so as to facilitate circulation and maintain the people's food supply. We are extremely grateful and anxious. Sincerely,

Reply Telegram from Zhejiang Province

Our Municipal Chamber of Commerce received a reply telegram from Chairman Huang of the Zhejiang Provincial Government yesterday, stating that, having read both telegrams, the province's rice production is not sufficient for self-sufficiency. All surplus rice from Wenzhou and Taizhou areas should be coordinated and regulated within the province. As for grain transported from Jiaxing to Shanghai, it should be handled prudently within a reasonable limit, based on the previous exchange of documents and telegrams between your city and various organizations and groups. Sincerely,

Petition to the Ministry of Railways

Soybeans are the raw material for producing oilcake. Shandong, Henan, Anhui, and other provinces are the richest in soybean production. The factories in Shanghai rely on these provinces for their supply. We have received reports from our member association, Changde and other oil factories, stating that in recent months, soybeans and miscellaneous grains purchased from the production areas in Anhui province have been unable to be exported due to a lack of vehicles. At each station in Xuzhou, Bengbu, and Linhuaiguan, goods are piled up like mountains and cannot be exported. The source of supply to Shanghai is scarce, and factories are facing the risk of not having rice to cook. The market price of soybeans and grains has also continued to rise as a result. Moreover, the accumulation of goods will inevitably lead to mold and spoilage, and the stagnation of finances will cause difficulties in turnover, which will affect commerce. This is no trivial matter. If no measures are taken to dredge this situation, panic will appear immediately. The aforementioned situation is factual. We are now submitting this document to your ministry, requesting that you promptly order the stations in Xuzhou, Bengbu, and Lingguan to allocate vehicles and give priority to exporting the stockpiled soybeans and miscellaneous grains, in order to clear the accumulated goods, facilitate transport to Shanghai, and maintain commerce. We would be immensely grateful. Sincerely,

Support for Suiyuan from All Sectors; Grain Organizations

Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, bean and rice merchants and various grain organizations from Guangdong, Hubei, Chaozhou, Shantou, Fujian, Zhenjiang, and other regions held an emergency meeting on the third floor of the Grain and Oilcake Traders Association on Minquan Road. Over twenty committee members attended, including Chen Ziyi, Zhu Zixiang, He Zisheng, Jiang Hongbin, Cai Yukun, Chuan Changyu, Ye Hongfan, and Gan Yuming. Gu Xinyi chaired the meeting, with Kong Ruling as the recorder. After the customary formalities, the chairman first reported on the situation of the bandits and puppets invading Suiyuan, and the heroic suppression by Chairman Fu and his troops. A resolution was immediately passed to establish a Grain Industry Support Suiyuan Fundraising Committee, and the committee members of eight grain organizations were appointed as ex officio members. These are (Bean) Cuixiu Hall, (Rice) Rengu Hall, (Guangdong) Shenshou Hall, (Hubei) Zhicheng Hall, (Chaozhou) Chaozhou Sugar and Sundries Trade Association, (Shantou) Quanzhang Guild Hall and Jin Hui Guild Hall, (Fujian) Sanshan Guild Hall, (Zhenjiang) Jiyuan Hall. A fundraising campaign among the industry will begin soon. The rationale for the fundraising is as follows: (Omitted above) Suiyuan is a vital national defense fortress. The gains and losses of Suiyuan are related to the survival of North China. Its importance cannot be overstated. Fortunately, our Chairman Fu and his generals deeply understand this great significance, vowing to defend our borders. Fighting fiercely through snowy nights, shedding blood on the yellow sands, fighting for the survival of the nation, and adding glory to the country. Their spirit is high in the cold wind. News of their victories spread frequently and excited the whole country. We, the grain industry colleagues, are all Chinese descendants, with our own families and businesses. Saving the country is saving ourselves. We cannot lag behind. Donating airplanes to serve the country, we have exhausted our meager efforts. At this time when soldiers are dying on the battlefield, it is time for us to destroy our homes to help the country. Therefore, we gathered at this meeting to discuss and implement plans together. We hope that our colleagues will act swiftly and enthusiastically donate. We must urgently comfort the soldiers who are fighting in the frozen land, and we must protect and rescue the compatriots who have suffered the brutality of the bandits. The rise and fall of the nation hangs by a thread, and our benevolence and righteousness lie here. This is our appeal. A telegram was also sent to Chairman Fu, saying: "Chairman Fu of Suiyuan, please forward this to the frontline generals to note: The bandits and puppets have invaded. Fortunately, we rely on you and your generals to bravely fight and severely damage the enemy. Your righteous reputation has spread, and everyone admires you. We hope that you will continue your efforts and firmly defend our territory. Our colleagues will surely economize on food and clothing and do our best to help. We send this telegram to comfort you, and look forward to your great achievements."

29th Squadron

The officers and members of the 29th Squadron of the 5th Brigade of the Shanghai Civic Training Center, regarding the Suiyuan suppression of bandits, Squadron Leader Shen Zhenwan has made great efforts to advocate and raise funds for assistance. They have unanimously economized on food and clothing and raised 273 yuan in national currency, which has been delivered to this newspaper to be sent to the front lines for comfort.

Lace Embroidery Industry

The Shanghai Lace and Drawnwork Industry Association is organizing fundraising to support Suiyuan, stating: "The bandits and puppets are invading the border, and the situation in Suiyuan is serious. National sovereignty and the lives of the people are of utmost importance. In the depths of winter, snow flies on the border, and the cold is piercing. The soldiers on the front lines endure the cold and fight against the enemy, and the people are bleeding, sacrificing their lives for the country, fighting for the survival of the people and preserving the integrity of the territory. We are deeply moved and admire their determination. Patriotic people who hear of this are shocked and are rushing to provide comfort, destroy their homes to help the country, encourage and assist, all sharing the same sentiment. Our colleagues in the industry must not ignore this. We must urgently help each other and act as a backing to boost the morale of the soldiers. This is of utmost importance." Shanghai Lace and Drawnwork Industry Association, November of the Republic of China Year.

Women's Organizations

The Shanghai Women's Circle Suiyuan Bandit Suppression Comfort Association held its first executive committee meeting yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM. Over thirty people attended, including Jin Guangmei, Wu Deyi, Cai Jinying, Yan Zhenyu, Jiang Huiro, Zhu Zhixue from the Women's Progressive Association; Lin Kecong from the Municipal Women's Association; Tu Kunfan from the Women's Relief Association; Lu Weiming and Zhao Wenqi from the Women's Lifestyle Improvement Society; Zhenhua and Chen Zhujun from the Chinese Women's Society. Tu Kunfan chaired the meeting, and Jiang Huiro recorded. After discussion, the following resolutions were made: (1) Send representatives to factories to solicit donations. All donations should be sent directly to the designated banks. (2) Send representatives to various theaters and venues to solicit donations. (3) Broadcast propaganda on the radio to support Suiyuan. (4) Launch a "One Cent a Day Savings" campaign, and all members of the affiliated associations should promote and implement it.

YWCA

The Shanghai YWCA on Jing'an Temple Road convened a meeting of its Executive Board yesterday at noon to discuss how to lead all the women in the city to provide support for Suiyuan and promote the nation's full efforts to relieve the disaster and fulfill their obligations. At that time, a consensus was reached on the following methods: (1) Support the soldiers; (2) Provide relief to wounded soldiers and refugees. The plan is divided into the following tasks: One, to solicit members of the Society who are willing to sacrifice their time for the country, and all women in the city, to come to the Society to make items for the soldiers, wounded soldiers, and refugees, such as cotton vests, ropes, quilts, and cloth. The working hours are temporarily set for every day from 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM, except for Sundays. All those who wish to participate can register at the Society. One, to collect donations and objects daily (Donations can be used to purchase items for soldiers and wounded soldiers, such as gas masks, food, etc.). The collection point is located at 996 Jing'an Temple Road, Shanghai YWCA, telephone number 34924.

New China Medical College

The New China Medical College on Wangjiasha launched a fundraising campaign to provide comfort. It stipulates that teachers and staff should donate at least one-thirtieth of their monthly salary, and students should donate at least 30 cents each, with no limit on larger donations. Enthusiastically making donations, they have already raised about 200 yuan. Furthermore, the president and vice-president of the college, Zhu Nanshan and Zhu Hegao, have initiated a campaign among the city's doctors of traditional Chinese medicine to donate the income from one day's consultations as a consolation fund. This has been submitted to the Chinese Medicine Association for approval and implementation.

Colleagues at the Exhibition Hall

All colleagues at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Commodity Exhibition Hall economized on food for one day yesterday (each person can save 20 cents in national currency) and handed over the saved funds to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to be sent to the front lines, to boost morale.

Guangming Thermos Factory

Workers enthusiastically support Suiyuan, Qingyun. Guangming Thermos and Electrical Appliance Manufacturing has worked hard on national products for more than ten years. The colleagues in the factory are particularly enthusiastic about patriotism. This time, the bandits and puppets invaded the border, and the war in Suiyuan broke out. The factory workers immediately launched a campaign to donate one day's worth of food expenses to support the army. They have now collected 136 yuan and 9 cents, which has been delivered to the Newspaper Office for transfer to the front lines.

Zhongfa Pharmacy

In addition to donating a percentage of the day's business income, all employees have also donated their daily salary income to contribute to the country. It has been decided to send this donation, along with more than a hundred pieces of important medicines, to the front lines to encourage morale.

Jiang Yiping and Others

Lawyers Jiang Yiping, Zhang Shiying, and Wang Peiyuan invited many well-known lawyers and educators from this city to the International Hotel the other evening. During the dinner, Lawyer Jiang initiated a game of finger-guessing and ordering to gamble with national currency. Those who lost contributed money to avoid being punished with wine. The collected funds were all donated to the Suiyuan anti-Japanese soldiers. In one hour, 300 yuan was collected. Because Lawyer Dong Chi and his wife were not good at drinking, they contributed the most money, accounting for 140 yuan. Jiang Yiping and his wife donated 70 yuan, Xia Anxiu and his wife donated 40 yuan, and Zhang Yifan, Zhang Shiying, Hua Maosheng, Tang Shizhen, and Wang Peiyuan donated 10 yuan each, totaling 300 yuan. It has been handed over to Shen Bao's consolation fund donation office to forward to the front lines.

Wuxi Native Place Association

The Wuxi Shanghai Native Place Association recently held an emergency meeting yesterday afternoon, given the critical situation with bandits and puppets invading the northern border of Suiyuan, to discuss ways to provide relief to the loyal and brave soldiers on the front lines. It was decided to notify the Wuxi natives residing in Shanghai to enthusiastically make donations, and designated the Nantao Commercial Bank, Penglai Bank, Xijin Public Office, and the association as collection points, so as to concentrate the funds and hand them over to the Suiyuan Rear Support Association for relief.

Mr. Dai Anguo and Miss Tang Meizhen Hold a Grand Wedding

Dai Anguo, son of Dai Chuanxian, Central Committee Member and President of the Examination Yuan, held his wedding ceremony yesterday at the Cangzhou Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road. The bride is Miss Tang Meizhen, the eldest daughter of Tang Jingyuan, the chief editor of the Shibao newspaper. Mr. Dai studied in Germany for nine years and returned to China this year. Miss Tang is a graduate of Qiming Girls' School, excelling in both character and academics. This marriage between Dai and Tang was arranged by Niu J'ian and Zhou Liangcheng, uniting a talented man and a beautiful woman in a blessed union. The parents of both sides, considering the national crisis, did not want to be extravagant, so they did not send out wedding invitations beforehand. However, on this auspicious day, relatives and friends came to offer their congratulations, forming a very lively gathering. Guests included Kong Xiangxi, Sun Ke, Li Shizeng, Chen Tiaoyuan, Chen Lifu, Wu Tiecheng, Yang Hu, Cai Jingjun, Xu Kan, Yu Hede, Wang Xiaolai, Qian Yongming, Du Yong, Zhang Yin, Yao Zong, Guan Jiong, Wang Yiting, Qu Yingguang, and hundreds of others. Generalissimo Chiang and his wife, as well as Song Ziwen, He Yingqin, Zhang Renjie, Cai Yuanpei, Yu Youren, Zhou Zuomin, Zhang Daofan, Yu Feipeng, and others, sent valuable gifts. The wedding ceremony was held at 4:00 PM, with Zhang Zhizhong and Zhu Jiahua as the best men. The banquet started at 6:00 PM, accompanied by entertainment, toasts and exchanges of cups, and the guests enjoyed themselves and dispersed.

Photograph of the Wedding of Mr. Dai and Miss Tang (Wang Kai Photograph)

German Ambassador Went to Beijing Yesterday

German Ambassador to China, Dr. Trautmann, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing several days ago. He did not have any special mission for this visit, but he visited Huang Fu at the Hong En Hospital, where he was received by Mrs. Huang. The ambassador returned to Beijing by train last night.

Yesterday, telegrams were sent separately to慰勞金 them as follows: (1) To Chairman Chiang in Luoyang: The bandits disturbed Suiyuan East. Thanks to our soldiers who bravely suppressed them, they were able to be pacified. However, their arrival has its origins, so they will inevitably invade again. You have come to guide and your efforts are strenuous. At this time, all parties are angry, and we only hope to wield our spears and destroy them, permanently securing our country. Shanghai Pudong Association's New Clubhouse Inauguration Ceremony and Opening of the 5th General Assembly Yesterday

Yesterday, the Pudong Association's new clubhouse on Rue Edouard (east end of Chengdu Road) was inaugurated. The ceremony was held at 10:00 AM, followed by entertainment starting at 2:00 PM. Approximately 10,000 guests and fellow villagers attended. Details are recorded as follows:

Attendees

Yesterday's attendees included Mayor Wu, Tao Baichuan, Cai Jingguo, Lu Jingshi, Wang Xiaolai, Yu Qiaqing, Zhang Binghui, Gu Xinyi, Du Chongyuan, Yuan Ludeng, Shen Junru, Yu Zuoting, Jin Tingxun, Lu Bohong, and others. Over 20,000 members arrived successively. Du Hall, as well as the halls on the sixth floor like Yi Hall, Chuansha Hall, Water Conservancy Hall, and Guanghua Hall, were all packed, extremely lively. Association directors and supervisors Pan Zhiwen, Chen Zixin, Zhu Shaoyi, Zhu Yunzhang, Mu Wenyun, Gu Wensheng, Yu Zhenhui, Pan Hongding, Jin Hongxiang, Zhai Shao Yi, Zhang Bochu, Gong Huibai, Jia Jinfang, Cai Jun Tu, Xing Zhigang, Han Shangde, Tao Qinwen, and others served as hosts. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and the Scout troop of Sze Sheng Middle School were present to maintain order, which was quite helpful. Additionally, the Pui Yik Vocational School and the Soochow General Hospital military bands provided entertainment, which was very orderly.

Opening Ceremony Order

At 10:00 AM, music was played and firecrackers were set off. Zhang Qizhi presented the key, and Chairman of the Standing Committee Du Yuesheng opened the door. Music was played. Standing Committee members Mu Ouchu, Huang Renzhi, and Lü Yuequan raised the flags. After Mayor Wu Tiecheng unveiled the plaque, music was played to start the meeting. Du, Mu, Huang, and Lü, along with Standing Committee member Shen's representative Pan Zhiwen, supervisors Lin Kang, Qin Yanqi, Wang Yiting, and Chen Taoyi, formed the presidium. Gu Wensheng served as the master of ceremonies, and Cai Jun Tu and Yu Zhenhui served as the recorders. The ceremony proceeded as planned. Chairman of the Standing Committee Du reported that many guests from various sectors had come to participate in the inauguration ceremony of the Pudong Association. The people of Pudong were very grateful. There are many people from Pudong in Shanghai, but only now do we have a Pudong Association address. The people of Pudong are truly ashamed. Now that the people of Pudong have a clubhouse for the association, we should work hard to connect emotionally with fellow villagers and to develop local businesses in Pudong. The Chinese people have particularly good feelings towards their fellow villagers. Every province and region has its own association. With a fellow villager organization, fellow villagers will no longer be scattered like sand, and only then can we unite. Now that China's national crisis is urgent, if the fellow villager associations in various provinces and regions can connect and form a large united organization, it would be a large fellow villager association of the Republic of China, unanimously resisting foreign aggression and not being bullied by others. Today, the Pudong Association is holding a meeting, and guests from all walks of life have come here. Thank you very much. If the hospitality is not good enough, please forgive our neglect.

Mayor Wu's Speech

Mayor Wu's speech stated: "Ladies and gentlemen, today the Pudong Association is holding the inauguration ceremony of its new clubhouse. I am deeply honored to be able to participate in this grand event and to unveil the plaque. The completion of the new Pudong Association clubhouse can be said to be the foundation of Shanghai's enterprise and also the foundation of Shanghai's future prosperity. Because Pudong is one of the important areas of Shanghai, and it produces many talented people, many social leaders are from Pudong. They all compete to be first in public welfare undertakings and are eager to do good. Therefore, the people of Pudong have made great achievements in Shanghai's undertakings. Now that the new Pudong Association clubhouse is completed, the unity will be even more consolidated, and the development of local undertakings will be further promoted. Therefore, I say that it is the foundation of Shanghai's enterprise and also the foundation of future prosperity. The organization of the fellow villager association is to show sincerity, unity, and mutual assistance. In today's society, we must not be like 'chickens and dogs not hearing each other,' and we must not 'sweep the snow from our own doorstep.'"

Speeches from Various Sectors

Next, Tao Baichuan delivered a speech, stating that the essence of organizing a fellow villager association is nothing more than connecting feelings and seeking local welfare. The establishment of the Pudong Association demonstrates the greatness of the spirit of unity among the people of Pudong. Then, Zhang Binghui delivered a speech on behalf of Director Pan, stating that there are many fellow villager associations, but the Pudong Association is particularly sound. With this foundation, it will be able to assume the responsibility of stabilizing the country in the future. Then, Wang Xiaolai gave a speech, stating that in the past, fellow villager associations were guilds and public offices, but they mostly focused on passively handling charitable and public welfare affairs. The Pudong Association is a rising star, which is truly admirable. Then, Jiang Wenyu gave a speech, stating that the Pudong Association has a great spirit and a brand-new construction, integrating material and spiritual aspects into one. This is due to the excellent members leading in the front and the sound members assisting in the rear. What is especially admirable is that they can extend from fellow villagers to all mankind, which can be said to have a true spirit of serving society. Then, Huang Renzhi gave a thank-you speech, first expressing gratitude to the party and government representatives and guests, and then encouraging the people of Pudong with four points: (1) The people of Pudong must constantly seek to increase their knowledge and abilities. (2) The people of Pudong must do their duty in a down-to-earth manner. (3) The people of Pudong must abandon private views and private interests, unite and serve the public, serve the country, and serve all mankind. (4) The people of Pudong must strive forward and develop the spirit of daily renewal. After the speech, music was played and the meeting adjourned.

Entertainment and Visits

There were a large number of attendees that day. Fortunately, the eight-story building allowed guests and members to visit separately, so the order was still quite orderly. At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, entertainment began. The programs in Du Hall included Deng Guoqing's amazing skills, the Tongzi Feixuan troupe's novel art, Zhang Qiaonong and Xu Lingling's jokes and humor, and martial arts performances. In Yi Hall on the sixth floor, there were silk and bamboo music and local dramas, etc., full of energy and enthusiasm, greatly increasing the interest of the audience. At 8:00 PM, there was Peking opera, all performed by famous amateur performers and ladies, which was also very exciting. At 12:00 PM, there was also Sichuan opera. Since the association had many guests and members, Zhai Jun specially formed a rescue team, with interns from Sheng Sheng Hospital and students from Sheng Sheng School taking on the duties. For lunch, the Pudong Friendship Dining Association held a dinner, which members praised as convenient.

New Life Movement Conference Decides on Principles to Abolish Extra Gratuities; Labor and Management of Various Industries to Formulate Methods; Scheduled to Implement Starting January 1, 1937

The Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association convened the fifth meeting yesterday, gathering relevant industries, labor, and management to continue discussing the abolition of extra gratuities.

Attendees

Attendees included Jiang Hao, secretary of the New Life Movement Promotion Association; Zhu Weichang of the Motor Vehicle Drivers' Union; Zhang Daxin of the Yunfei Motor Vehicle Drivers' Union; Li Mancun of the Restaurant Industry Association; Zhan Wenxi, Yao Songping, Sun Qiuping, Gao Weifu, Zhang Zhicheng, Xia Tingliang, Li Sichao, Zou Juncheng of the Hotel Industry Association; and Xie Renchen, a representative of the Social Affairs Bureau, etc. Chairman Jiang Hao reported on the progress and current situation of the abolition of extra gratuities, hoping that the industries would formulate a feasible implementation plan based on the methods and principles agreed upon by the General Assembly. After discussion, it was decided that before December 25 of this year, detailed methods should be discussed and agreed upon by labor and management of various industries based on the four principles formulated and submitted to the association for review, so that they could be implemented starting on January 1, 1937.

Agreed Principles

(1) Workers in various industries should determine their wages. For those who have not yet determined their wages, the standards should be negotiated separately by labor and management of each company and reported to the municipal government for record. (2) The temporary collection of gratuities should be based on the principle that the majority belongs to the labor side. The distribution method should be negotiated by labor and management. (3) Large guarantee deposits should be replaced by shop guarantees in the future. If there are special circumstances and cash must be collected, it should be deposited in a reliable bank and interest should be paid according to regulations. (4) Workers are absolutely not allowed to solicit gratuities from customers in the future.

Accused of Stealing a Letter, Zhang Zhifan Acquitted and Released

The Guohua Obstetrics Hospital at No. 134 Kunming Road is run by the brothers Zhang Wenxing and Zhang Zhifan from Fujian. Before the 29th of last month, a registered letter was sent from Xiashi to the hospital. The letter stated that it should be received by Di Shilin, a female nurse in the hospital, and transferred to Wang Manying. The sender was Wang Manying's younger brother. The letter also included a small remittance of ten yuan. However, Di did not receive the letter. Wang Manying inquired with Di, but there was no result. She reported it to the police. After investigation by the post office, it was discovered that the return receipt for the letter had the Guohua Hospital seal on it, and Zhu Wenyi, an inspector of the bureau, testified that the seal on the return receipt was affixed by Zhang Zhifan. The police arrested Zhang Zhifan and handed him over to the First Special Court, which filed a public prosecution against him for theft and obstructing secrecy. He was detained for interrogation. Yesterday morning, Judge Dai Rongduo opened the Fifth Criminal Court for a new trial. Police lawyer Jiang Baolian presented the case and questioned Zhang Zhifan, who denied receiving the letter. As for the seal, it was affixed by the post office to make up for it. He did not know whether he had received the letter before. He hired lawyer Yang Ruinian to defend him. After Judge Dai verified the statements, he acquitted and released Zhang Zhifan in court.

Counterfeiting Japanese Ten-Sen Coins, One Criminal Commits Suicide by Poison, Li Yunshi's Body Autopsied Yesterday, Remaining Liquid Sent to Municipal Council for Analysis, Another Criminal Zhu Xing San Denies Counterfeiting

At 10:00 AM the day before yesterday, two Japanese detectives were dispatched by the Japanese Consulate to report to the Hongkou Police Station, stating that there were two Chinese people counterfeiting Japanese ten-sen coins. The location was at No. 52, Lane 172, Kunyou Road. The police station dispatched Western Detective Aiertsi and Chinese Detective No. 157 to secretly go to the address. They found two people, Li Yunshi (47 years old) from Nanjing and Zhu Xingshan (44 years old) from Shandong, and found 30 counterfeit ten-sen coins at the site. They were all taken back to the police station. After questioning, they learned the location of the counterfeit coin factory. The detectives took the two defendants to the residence of Yun Zhi at No. 14 Shunchang Lane, Jumen Road in Nanshi. They found several small packages of metal materials. At that moment, Li suddenly took a can of liquid poison from the window sill and swallowed it. The detective urgently stopped him, but Li's face turned pale and he foamed at the mouth. The detectives sent him to Shanghai Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective and he died. The body was taken to the autopsying place on Feilun Road to await autopsy. The detectives brought the liquid and other items back to the police station. Yesterday morning, Zhu Xingsan was first sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court and was approved to be detained. Then, the Procuratorate of the Court was requested to commission Prosecutor Tang to conduct an autopsy with forensic doctors Wei and Zhang, and Clerk Wang Zuyi. The autopsy confirmed the body. According to Chinese Head Constable Xu Shunqing, the case was reported to the Japanese Consulate by a Japanese informant. It was then known that the family of the informant was on Kunshan Road. On the 10th of this month, the two defendants took 30 counterfeit ten-sen coins to that place as samples. They went again yesterday and were arrested. When the deceased took the poison, he was pointing at the evidence and took it before anyone could stop him. According to Zhu Xingsan, he lives at No. 478 Qingshun Lane, Bai'er Road and works as a customs broker. He met the deceased in February or March of this year. He went to Qishan Road that day to collect commissions and denied counterfeiting ten-sen coins. Prosecutor Tang, after hearing the statements and the autopsy, determined that the deceased Li Yunshi, male, died of poison. Before the family members are identified, the body will be sent to the Pushan Villa for safekeeping. In order to clarify the name of the liquid poison, Tang ordered the police station to send it to the Municipal Council for analysis and ordered that the body be temporarily kept out of the coffin or dissected.

The Truth About the Murder of the Owner of Hongxing Tobacco and Paper Store: Li Gensheng's Concubine Suddenly Disappears, Suspected of Being Hidden by the Store Owner, So He Went to Avenge, Two Murderers Detained Pending Rescheduled Interrogation

The wife of Kuang Hongsheng, the owner of Hongxing Tobacco and Paper Grocery Store at No. 1182 Gordon Road, works as a female foreman at the Tongyi Yarn Factory on Mozishan Road. However, one of the female workers, Aidi, is the concubine of Li Gensheng from Ningbo. This time, Aidi was laid off from work and disappeared. Li Gensheng suspected that Kuang and his wife were hiding her and held a grudge. He wanted to harm them, so he discussed revenge with Yao Ronggen and Wang Jinshan, two locals living at No. 21 Dunmu Lane, Guoqing Road, Zhabei. Zhang provided the guns and bullets. At around 11:00 PM the night before last, they went to the Hongxing Tobacco and Paper Store together. Li Gensheng took out a gun and fired a shot, hitting Kuang Hongsheng in the left brain. Li was about to continue firing, but the bullet jammed, so he could not continue. He turned around and fled in different directions. At that time, a Chinese policeman No. 1941 was on duty at the intersection of Gordon Road and Robert Road. He suddenly heard gunshots and saw Li Gensheng running, so he chased after him. Li knew he was defeated and quickly threw away the gun, but was still caught and the gun and bullets were recovered. At the same time, Chinese policemen No. 3266 and No. 85 also heard the shouts and saw Wang Jinshan running away, so they chased and caught him. Chinese policemen No. 3396 and No. 3221 saw the owner of Hongxing Tobacco and Paper Store, Kuang Hongsheng, lying in a pool of blood, so they took him to the police station and ordered the injured to be sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. Detective Jia Di was in charge of the investigation. Based on the confession of the captured criminals, the location of Yao Ronggen's hiding place was discovered. Police detectives from the Public Security Bureau went to No. 21 Dunmu Lane, Guoqing Road and arrested Yao. At that time, Yao was wearing a No. 8 uniform from the Daguangming Cinema. He was detained in the Public Security Bureau pending transfer. Yesterday morning, Li and Wang were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court and prosecuted for attempted murder under Article 271, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. Police lawyer Wang Yaoxun rose and presented the case, stating that after the victim Kuang Hongsheng was sent to the hospital, the doctor confirmed that he was injured in the left shoulder and the bullet had exited the lungs. He was seriously injured and his life was in danger. Therefore, after arresting the defendants, Li Gensheng admitted that he fired the gun. Wang Jinshan initially denied it, so Li was taken to Renji Hospital, where Kuang clearly identified him as the perpetrator. Kuang's life or death is uncertain, so he requested a postponement and requested a document to be issued to the police station to transfer Yao Ronggen from the Public Security Bureau for a joint interrogation. He presented the recovered guns, bullets, bullet casings, etc. Kuang Hongsheng stated that Aidi is my concubine. This time, she disappeared because she was hidden by Kuang and taken to another place. Therefore, last night, he invited Wang and Yao to find Aidi. The gun was provided by Yao. At that time, he only threatened Kuang. Unexpectedly, Kuang stepped forward to grab it, so he fired a shot at him, hitting Kuang in the left chest. Wang Jinshan confessed to going with him, but only acted as a lookout at the door. Judge Huang Risheng ordered the two defendants to be detained for a rescheduled interrogation in seven days.

Substitute for Dancing Girls: Embezzlement of Engagement Money Leads to Punishment; Original Thief Found with Money in His Trousers Pocket; Xiao Peilin Sentenced to Fifty Days of Detention

Li Te, a Korean manager of the Cathay Dance Hall in Hong Kong, recently came to Shanghai with a Chinese man named Yan Lanting to recruit dancing girls. They stayed in Room 311 of the New World Hotel. At that time, they entrusted Xiao Peilin, a Ningbo native and president of the Art Sea Dancing Research Institute at No. 14 Daqing Lane, Nanjing Road, to find suitable candidates. Soon, Xiao claimed to have found three dancers from the Vienna Dance Hall: Zhang Bixia, Zhang Qingying, and Pan Jiaoli. He showed their photos to Li Te, but said that each girl required an upfront settlement fee of 30 yuan before agreeing to go. Li Te paid the full amount. Later, Xiao also invited Lu Ying and Fang Mei, female employees of the Metropolitan Guide Agency, to Li's room, encouraging them to go to Hong Kong as dancing partners. Lu and the others agreed, but also requested a settlement fee of 30 yuan each. Li Te then paid Xiao 10 yuan, instructing him to forward it, with the remaining 20 yuan to be paid upon departure. However, after Xiao received the 130 yuan from Li, he did not distribute it to the dancers and disappeared. Later, Li encountered him on the street and had him detained at the New Zha Police Station, from where he was brought to the First Special District Court for interrogation. The case was awaiting sentencing. Yesterday morning, Ye Shengchao, a judge, took the stand in the Second Criminal Court. Qian Xunjiu, a lawyer from the police station, immediately requested a retrial, arguing that during the previous hearing, the defendant completely denied receiving any money from Li Te. After the court declared the hearing closed, while the defendant was being escorted to the waiting room, 40 Hong Kong dollars and 20 dollars in Shandong China Communication Bank notes, totaling 60 yuan, were found in Xiao's trousers pocket. Li Te identified this as part of the money he had given to the defendant. According to Xiao, the money was hidden in the lining of his suit, so it was not found during the initial search. He thought there would be no further search after the hearing, so he took it out, only to have it discovered. Li Te testified that the money was indeed what he had paid. When questioned, Xiao continued to try to deny it, claiming it was given to him by a friend. Judge Ye sentenced Xiao to 50 days of detention and ordered the Hong Kong dollars to be returned to the plaintiff.

Navigation in Shanghai-Hankou Route: Draft Limited to Ten Feet

Wuhu Section Sets Shipping Regulations; Yangtze River Water Level Continues to Drop; Large Ships Suspend Operations; According to a Datong News Agency reporter, it was recently learned from the customs that the draft limit for ships on the Yangtze River from Shanghai to Hankou is 14 feet 4 inches from Wuhu to Jiujiang, and only 10 feet 5 inches from Jiujiang to Hankou. As the river water continues to recede daily, the impact on river transport is significant. Furthermore, the water fee for the Shanghai-Hankou line, which various shipping companies used to levy starting in February of the following year, will now be levied starting on the first of next month, indicating the unprecedented changes in the Yangtze River this year. In addition, the Wuhu section of the Shanghai-Hankou route is the narrowest and shallowest for navigation. Therefore, during this period of shallow water, the customs have specially formulated the following regulations based on the current situation: "Wuhu Channel" navigation guide: keep a distance of two chains from the shore, pass the Wuhu customs with the ship's bow pointing directly at the Wuhu Channel light pylon, approach the right bank and keep a distance of one chain from the shore. Follow this distance along the shore until reaching the Wuhu Channel light pylon, then take the route with the ship's starboard side half a ship's length away from the Qingyun lightship, and pass the lightship.

North Jiangsu Malaria Relief Team Returns to Shanghai; 100,000 Infected, Over 2,000 Cured

The Shanghai Nantong, Rugao, Chongming, Haimen, and Qidong Fellow Villagers Associations, due to the epidemic outbreak in Rugao this autumn, resulting in over 5,000 deaths, specially consulted with the Nanyang Hospital in Xiaodongmen to send eight doctors, including Gu Chengni, with Gu as the team leader, to organize a North Jiangsu Malaria Relief Team, carrying medicines to provide relief. The team has now completed its mission and returned to Shanghai. According to Mr. Gu yesterday, after arriving in Rugao, they worked with local health authorities in the most severely affected areas, such as XinYu, Yaowu, and WuXu in the eastern part of the county, Guba Town. In addition to sending two people to handle outpatient services daily, they also went to the countryside to provide relief. Of the 1.5 million people in the county, over 100,000 were infected. Over three weeks, they treated and cured over 2,000 people, spending 2,300 yuan on medicine. The most severe infection was malignant malaria. Because there were too many stagnant ponds in the area, breeding eternal mosquitoes, the transmission was the fastest. The fundamental solution is to dredge the water sources, allowing the stagnant ponds to interconnect with various rivers, making it easier to eradicate.

The Enamel Industry in Shanghai (A General Survey of Industry and Commerce in Shanghai - XXXVIII)

— Edited by China Investigation

1. Overview. The position of enamel products in our daily necessities has become increasingly important. For example, bowls and plates for eating and drinking, large and small basins and buckets for washing, and common signboards are mostly enamel products. The difference between enamel products and our country's traditional porcelain is that the former is made of iron sheets, while the latter is made of clay, so the degree of strength and fragility varies greatly. As for the enamel powder coated on the surface, it is actually no different from our country's porcelain.

The raw materials for enamel products are relatively simple, mainly enamel powder and iron sheets. In the past, enamel powder was purchased from Japan. Later, the Hetian Enamel Powder Pharmaceutical Factory, founded by the Japanese in Shanghai, also provided a large part. After the Chinese-owned Yifeng, Zhonghua, and Zhufeng enamel factories successively produced enamel powder themselves, this raw material was no longer controlled by the Japanese. However, the raw materials for manufacturing enamel powder, such as feldspar and clay, are still mostly dependent on Japan, which is a drawback. Although China produces feldspar and clay, they are rarely mined and remain hidden in nature. Therefore, we must continue to strive to mine this raw material in order to achieve the true independence of the enamel industry. As for iron sheets, because they are products of heavy industry, China is still unable to produce them domestically, and it is even more necessary for us to work hard.

The Kidnappers in the Xue Jiasheng Case Still Receive Original Sentence After Appeal; The Car Used by the Bandits Is Requested to Be Confiscated by the Police Station

Xue Jiasheng, a wealthy businessman living at No. 5, Lane 1412, Avenue Joffre, French Concession (the third son of the late Xue Baorun, a giant in the dyestuff industry), was kidnapped by bandits for ransom on August 1 this year at 4 PM. On August 15, the French police solved the case and arrested five kidnappers: Chen Jintang, Bu Mingqing, Pu Yaozhang, Sun Yanan, and Wu Genyou. They were handed over to the Second Special Court. The police department prosecuted and tried the case accordings to the law. Chen Jintang was sentenced to 15 years in prison and deprived of civil rights for 10 years. Bu Mingqing was sentenced to life imprisonment and deprived of civil rights for life. Wu Genyou was sentenced to 12 years in prison and deprived of civil rights for 10 years. Pu and Sun were found not guilty. Chen, Bu, and Wu appealed the verdict to the Third Branch of the High Court. Pu and Sun were released and regained their freedom after the police department abandoned the appeal. The appeal cases of Chen, Bu, and Wu were investigated several times by the Third Branch of the High Court, and the panel of judges summoned witnesses for trial. The details have been recorded in this publication. The case has now been concluded. Yesterday, Wu Tingqi, the head of the criminal court, along with judges Wang and Liao, rendered the verdict in the Third Criminal Court. The original judgment regarding Bu Mingqing was revoked. The crime was the same as in the first instance, but the words "repeat offender" were added. He was still sentenced to life imprisonment and deprived of civil rights for life. The appeals of Chen Jintang and Wu Genyou were rejected. After the sentence, the three criminals were ordered to be returned to the detention center. It is also reported that the car used to kidnap Xue was not seized when the case was solved because the bandits hid it. The detectives handling the case have now found the car and driven it back to the French police station. The police department has transferred it to the Second Special Court, requesting that the car be confiscated.
