Nankai Football Team played against Western Police in the Western League First Division match at Recreation Ground yesterday. After winning against St. Francis last week, Nankai, who had been sluggish for a long time, washed away their passive atmosphere and gradually became sharper and more active. With the well-coordinated team members, Nankai regained their inherent strength and felt invigorated. Western Police, after recently winning against St. Francis and the Western Chamber of Commerce, also had an unyielding spirit. Nankai was in high spirits, and the lively and active performance yesterday left Western Police at a loss. The first half ended in a 1-1 draw. In the end, Nankai won 4-2. However, the two goals conceded by Nankai were purely own goals, and Western Police did not achieve anything on their own.

Nankai Team

Ye Peichu

Chen Chunxiu, Xu Hongyin

Yan Lianjin, Chen Zhenxiang, Zhang Riyuan

Wang Nanzhen, Liu Yi, Shi Yongnan, Wu Shufen, Chen Mingzhi

Western Police Team

Mei Ying

Turner, Douglass

Helei, Wuiswood, Gibson

Willie, Wu Lei, Pete, Te Fei, Oklei

Deadlock

At the start, Western Police Beilei arrived late, with only ten players. Shi Yongnan dribbled the ball to attack. After a long melee, there was no progress. Beilei hurriedly arrived and joined the battle, gaining the upper hand. They dribbled the ball and attacked, firing a strong shot. Ye Peichu dived to save it. Oklei took a corner kick, landing the ball well. Ye bravely punched it out. Not long after, Beilei came back again, shooting fiercely from the right corner of the penalty area. Ye Peichu was quick and agile, saving it again. Under Nankai's fierce attack, Wang Nanzhen launched a surprise attack, advancing along the side. As the ball reached the center, Wu Shufen headed it forcefully. The ball hit Man Ying's body, and Chen Mingzhi rushed up to shoot again, but the ball hit the goalpost and bounced back, to no avail.

Each Scores One Goal

Before long, Chen Mingzhi rose up and Wang Nanzhen passed the ball to the center. Wu Shufen rushed up and shot fiercely. The goalkeeper was caught off guard, and the scoring was opened. Western Police did not give up and tried their best to counterattack. Willie Huite rose up in the middle and shot from the penalty area. Ye Peichu did not pay attention and casually caught it, but the ball had already crossed the goal line. A goal was unnecessarily lost, resulting in a draw. Only two minutes were left until the end of the first half.

Second Own Goal

After the break, Yan Lianjin and Wang Nanzhen coordinated well, penetrating deep into enemy territory. Wu Shufen had a flash of inspiration and shot at the goal. The enemy was caught off guard, and the ball went into the right corner of the goal, making it 2-1. Western Police suffered a setback and their troops were determined to avenge their humiliation. They turned around the battlefield, dribbling the ball forward. With Turner's support, they raised their foot to attack the goal. Xu Hongyin tried to be clever but ended up making things worse. He intended to block it, but unexpectedly scored an own goal, sacrificing another goal for no reason.

Two Goals in a Row

Western Police made something out of nothing, and their morale soared. Willie took a corner kick, which was perfectly placed. Oklei headed it directly, but fortunately, Ye Peichu turned the danger into safety. Wang Nanzhen launched another attack, and Liu Yi's header was successful, but it was a pity that it was not a goal. Liu refused to give up, and with Wu Shufen working together, they attacked the enemy. Wu Shufen had excellent ball luck and scored from 15 yards, making it 3-1. Finally, Chen Mingzhi advanced along the sideline and passed the ball to the center. Shi Yongnan rushed up and kicked the ball, which went into the net, making it 4-2. Although Western Police tried their best to resist, they were unable to achieve their wishes. The whistle blew to end the game, and Nankai achieved victory for the second time with a score of 4-2.

Chinese Football League, Group B: Guanghua Defeats Yousheng 4-1; Ten Matches Today

There was one match in the Chinese Football Association's Chinese Character Group yesterday, between Guanghua and Yousheng. It took place at 3:00 PM at the Guanghua University Stadium on Daxilu Road. Although Guanghua had lost to Fudan before, they had been practicing diligently recently and their lineup was visibly strengthened. Yousheng's skills were also quite respectable. However, because it was a community team, they lacked regular practice and were not as cohesive as a school team. As a result, Guanghua won 4-1. Guanghua won by two clear goals in the first half.

Two Important Matches in the Western League, Group B: Aurora and St. John's Struggle; Aurora Draws 3-3 with the French Army; St. John's Loses to the British Navy 1-2

In the Western League Group B matches yesterday, there were three matches involving Chinese teams, all of which were very important. The performances were also excellent and had a great impact on the prospects of winning the championship. As a result, Aurora drew 3-3 with the French Army, and St. John's lost 1-2 to the British Navy. The result of another match, Qinghua vs. Health, is unknown.

Aurora College

The team's skills are quite strong. Since the beginning of the season, they have never been defeated, and their hopes of winning the championship are very high. Yesterday, they fought the French Army at Hongkou Park Second Field. The competition between the two sides was extremely intense. The French army put up a stubborn resistance, and their momentum was very strong. Aurora was also careful and cautious, fighting aggressively. Each side achieved gains, resulting in a 3-3 draw. It is a pity that Aurora failed to win consecutive victories and lost a valuable point.

St. John's

Also a victorious team, determined to win the championship. Yesterday, they met the British Navy at Shen Garden, believing that it would not be difficult to win consecutive victories. However, the British soldiers who fought yesterday were from a newly arrived fleet, with considerable strength. They competed equally. In the first half, neither side scored. At the beginning of the second half, St. John's students made a mistake and were immediately scored on by the soldiers. St. John's tried its best to counterattack, and their momentum was very strong. The ball often revolved in front of the British soldiers' goal. Finally, after more than twenty minutes, they returned the goal, making it a 1-1 tie. After that, there were mutual scares, but both sides were able to protect their positions. They were full of hope that they would draw the match. Unexpectedly, in the last four minutes, they were suddenly scored on by the British army with a goal that decided the winner, ending with a score of 2-1.

Poor Coordination: Xin Team Loses to Xintong; Total Result: 43-32; Both Teams' Performances Lacked Distinctiveness

Xin Team's basketball team played a friendly match against Xintong Team, formerly known as Pirates, at Shen Garden last night. Both teams' performances lacked distinctiveness, their coordination was poor, and their movements were slow. The players of Xin Team were past their prime. If they want to improve, they must abandon their outdated style of play and undergo regular training. Xintong led all the way in the whole game. The first half ended 19-15. The final score was 43-32.

First Half

The situation in the first 20 minutes was relatively even. After the start, Xintong scored five consecutive points. Xin Team united and counterattacked, with Feng Nianhua, Xu Wenkui, and Chen Xianglong scoring successively, once leading 14-13. The situation was quite good. Xintong strengthened their defense, and Carson, Lam, Yu, and others scored several times. Pisai Er did not want to be left behind, and the score increased to 19 points. Xin Team only scored one point from Wenkui's free throw, making it 15-19. Xin Team was behind again.

Second Half

In a lackluster manner, Xintong relied on Rhine and Steguer's coordination to raise the score steadily. When it reached 34 points, Xin Team only had 16 points, which was scored by Sun Baoqing's free throw. Then Chen Xianglong put the ball in from under the basket. After Xiao Feng scored a free throw, Xu Wenkui made a wonderful long shot, and the momentum suddenly rose. Then Wenkui and Xianglong added three more points, showing great improvement. However, Xintong continued to work harder, and Rhine, Carson, and others frequently scored. In the end, Xin Team lost 32-43. The two teams will play a second match next Wednesday to decide the winner.

Education News

Cultural Circles' Aid-Sui Movement

The Cultural Aid-Sui Committee, organized by various cultural groups in the city, held its first executive meeting yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM at the China Cultural Construction Association. Those in attendance were Ku Hangbai, Chen Jicheng, Jiang Jianbai, Li Zhaohuan (representing Hu Xiongding), Fang Huanru (representing Huang Jingzhai), Liao Fangru, He Bingsong, Wang Boqi (representing Wang Weizhen), and Wang Yunwu (representing Gu Bingyuan). Tong Hangbai chaired the meeting, and Huang Jingzhai took the minutes. The following resolutions were made: (1) To confirm the membership of the committee: It was resolved that members of the Cultural Construction Association who attended the meeting would be members, and those who had not yet participated would be invited to join by letter from the committee. (2) To designate banks and organizations to collect donations: It was resolved to request the Bank of China, Central Bank, Bank of Communications, Shanghai Municipal Bank, and Shanghai banks to collect donations, and to ask Chen Jicheng to contact them. It was also resolved to request the Daily Newspaper Association and its member newspapers to collect donations, and to ask Wang Boqi to contact them. The donations will be deposited in the committee's account. (3) To print unified receipts to be issued by the committee: It was resolved to print three-part receipts to be distributed to the collecting banks and organizations. (4) To confirm the committee's internal organization: It was resolved that the executive committee would have a secretary-general and several staff members, who would be directed by the secretary-general. Jiang Jianbai was appointed as secretary-general. (5) To confirm the procedures for remitting donations: It was resolved that the remittance of donations must be approved by the committee and signed by Jiang Jianbai, He Bingsong, Wang Boqi, Liao Maoru, Wang Yunwu, Tong Hangbai, and Chen Jicheng (at least four signatures are required for remittance). (6) Regarding the delegation of fundraising teams proposed by the general assembly, it was resolved that the heads of each group and unit would be responsible for promoting everything. (7) To confirm the date of the regular meeting: It was resolved to hold a meeting every Friday at 4:00 PM, and to convene temporary meetings when necessary, which would be the responsibility of the secretary-general. (8) To confirm the location of the committee: It was resolved to set up the office at No. 500 Lafayette Road, inside the Cultural Construction Association. (9) To appoint the committee's accounting auditor: It was resolved to appoint Wu Yushu and Pan Xulun as voluntary accounting advisors. (10) To confirm the committee's expenses: It was resolved to hand the draft budget to the secretary-general and submit it to the next regular meeting for discussion and decision. (11) Regarding how to handle the reporting of donations: It was resolved to request that each collecting organization and bank report the receipt of the funds daily so that the committee can compile them and publish them in the newspapers daily. (12) Regarding the proposal by the general assembly that each unit should solicit donations from the outside world: It was resolved to start with the internal efforts of each unit first. (13) Regarding how to handle donations of goods: It was resolved to ask donors to notify the committee first so that staff can be sent to collect them. (14) Regarding the committee's proposal to send staff to the front lines to express sympathy: It was resolved to ask the secretary-general to contact other organizations to handle it.

Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Association held its second standing committee meeting of this semester at 10:00 AM on the 20th at the Provincial Zhenjiang Normal School. The attendees were Zhou Houchu, Liu Hengjing, Huang Zhifu, Zheng Xigu, Shao Heting, Cao Chu, Wang Junsheng, and others. Liu Hengjing chaired the meeting, and Cao Chu took the minutes. The standing committee first reported on (1) the presentation of gifts to the Provincial Government's Third Anniversary Celebration, (2) the contact with the Provincial Department regarding the supplementary payment of 10% for aircraft donations. Then, the discussion began, and the following resolutions were made: (1) How to comfort Chairman Fu Zuoyi and the soldiers on the front lines in Suiyuan: (Resolution) Send a telegram of encouragement. (2) Send a letter to all schools to encourage them to donate generously to comfort the soldiers. (3) Expand secondary education to help young people who have dropped out of school. The first general assembly passed three measures. How should they be implemented? (Resolution) Appoint Shao Heting, Zheng Xigu, and Cao Chu to formulate concrete measures, submit them to the next general assembly for approval, and present them to the department for adoption. (4) When should the second general assembly be held? (Resolution) It was decided that it would be held in mid-December.

The entire university department has also begun to promote "One Day of Exercise," "One Yuan of Exercise," and "Sunday Exercise" (i.e., saving all expendable money each week, such as travel expenses, movie fees, dining expenses, etc.), each contributing according to their ability to help the front lines so that the soldiers can fight the bandits for a long time.

The fundraising committee was formed by all the students and faculty and staff of the school and actively began to solicit donations from students, faculty, staff, and family and friends of students outside the school. Once the funds are raised, they will be remitted to the front lines to provide comfort.

As a result, the following resolutions were made: (1) To establish the Binhai Students' Aid-Suiyuan Bandits Suppression Association immediately. (2) All teachers and students of the school should save money on food and clothing to collect funds to comfort the soldiers on the front lines. (3) Furthermore, all teachers and students should solicit donations from relatives, friends, and neighbors to comfort the soldiers.

Crab South University The faculty, staff, students, and school workers of the University Department, Middle School Department, and Experimental School of National Jinan University, to comfort the soldiers guarding the border in Suiyuan and fighting the bandits, launched a campaign for faculty and staff to donate one day's salary, and students to solicit donations by grade. Number of National Academic Institutions and Groups Increased: Institutions Increased by 10, Groups Increased by 35

The Ministry of Education recently compiled statistics on major academic institutions and groups nationwide. As of the end of October this year, compared with the statistics in 1934, the number of institutions increased by 10 and the number of groups increased by 35. Compared with the total number of 144 institutions and groups in 1934, the number is now 189, an increase of 45. The distribution by category is as follows:

Distribution Status: There are 10 institutions and 59 groups in Nanjing, and institutions and 46 groups in Shanghai. There are 4 institutions and 10 groups in Beiping, 8 institutions and 1 group in Jiangsu, 1 institution and 6 groups in Fujian, 2 institutions and 5 groups in Shandong, 4 institutions in Jiangxi, 3 institutions in Hunan, 1 institution and 2 groups in Hubei, 3 groups in Zhejiang, 3 groups in Qingdao, 1 institution and 1 group each in Henan and Shanxi, 1 group each in Anhui, Suiyuan, and Weihaiwei, and 1 institution each in Hebei, Shaanxi, Guangxi, and Guangzhou. There is 1 group in Tianjin. The total is 45 institutions and 144 groups, totaling 189. Category of Subjects: (1) "General Category": 27, accounting for 18.75%. (2) "Practical Category": Medicine and Pharmacy 18, accounting for 12.50%, Engineering 12, accounting for 8.33%, Science 11, accounting for 7.64%, Agriculture and Forestry 5, accounting for 3.47%. The total of practical categories is 46, accounting for 31.94%. (3) "Liberal Arts Category": Social Sciences 25, accounting for 17.36%, Education 22, accounting for 15.28%, Literature and Art 14, accounting for 9.72%. The total of liberal arts categories is 61, accounting for 42.36%. (4) "Physical Education and Youth Category": 10, accounting for 6.95%. Comparing the above categories, the general category is the most, followed by social sciences, and social sciences are dominated by political economy, which is somewhat abnormally developed. Agriculture is the least. China is founded on agriculture, but there are fewer people studying agriculture. It is up to educators to think about promoting agriculture in order to save the situation in case of emergency.

Shanghai University's 20th Anniversary Grand Occasion (International News Agency)

Shanghai University 30th Anniversary Ceremony - Minister of Education Wang and Mayor Wu Both Attended and Gave Instructions

Shanghai Hujiang University held its 30th anniversary ceremony at 3:00 PM yesterday. Attendees included Minister of Education Wang, Director Lei, Shanghai Mayor Wu, former President of the Judicial Yuan Dr. Wang Chonghui, and over 2,000 guests from all walks of life, parents of students, and alumni. A detailed account of the event is as follows:

Campus Decorations

From the school gate to the auditorium, an archway decorated with pine and cypress and hung with red lanterns stood every few dozen steps. Between the auditorium and the science building stood a magnificent and ornate "Fraternity" archway donated by the student association. The Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau's military band began playing music at 7:00 AM yesterday to maintain order. Boy Scouts were on hand to greet guests, all of whom were school faculty and staff. The corridors and reception rooms of the auditorium were adorned with gifts from various sectors, a dazzling display that was a feast for the eyes.

Ceremony Program

Yesterday was the second day of the anniversary celebration. At 8:00 AM, there was a review of military training students and Boy Scouts. At 10:00 AM, a football match was held between middle and high schools. At 12:30 PM, alumni lined up, followed by an alumni celebration banquet at 1:00 PM. The anniversary ceremony began at 3:00 PM, presided over by President Liu. The meeting commenced with the usual formalities, followed by an address from President Liu. Next, Minister of Education Wang delivered a speech, expressing his hope that Hujiang University would be able to shoulder the mission of an ideal university, becoming (1) an excellent teaching institution, (2) an academic research institution, and (3) a character training institution, continuing its efforts of the past 30 years and striving for glorious development in the future. Shanghai Mayor Wu then gave a speech, urging young people to use the intelligence and abilities of a few to prepare to solve the survival problems of the majority in the future. He emphasized that the important principle is to seek knowledge at school, not to seek personal advancement, and to work together for the self-improvement of the country and the nation, so that the country and the nation can find a proper way out, and at the same time, the personal way out will also be solved. Following this, guests and alumni delivered speeches one after another, praising the school and offering much encouragement. Finally, President Liu gave a thank-you speech. At 5:00 PM, there was a tea party to entertain guests, which was also an alumni reunion. At 7:00 PM, there was a variety show, and at 7:30 PM, a broadcast was made on the gospel radio station, broadcasting anniversary news.

Various Exhibitions

During the anniversary celebration, the school held various exhibitions for the guidance of guests. The physics, chemistry, and biology department exhibitions were held in the science building, the art exhibition in the library, the calligraphy exhibition in the Sifei Hall, the high and junior middle school achievement exhibition in the affiliated middle school, and the elementary school exhibition in the elementary school department. At the same time, middle school teacher Wu Fuzhi also held a personal painting exhibition in the middle school auditorium.

Publication Giveaways

Yesterday, guests who came to the school received publications as souvenirs and to express gratitude. These included "Tianniao Quarterly," "Science Special Issue," "Horn Sound," and "Anniversary Special Issue," among others.

Investigation of Kangjia Elementary School

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, upon discovering that Kangjiaqiao Kangjia Elementary School in Caojiadu, West Shanghai, had violated educational regulations, failed to register with the authorities, and even dared to raise funds externally, ordered the police to seal the school on the 6th of last month. Unexpectedly, the principal of the school, Chen Guohua, secretly unsealed the school on the 17th of this month and resumed classes as usual. After Director Pan discovered this, he immediately dispatched police to the school and arrested teachers Yu Jian and Zha Changji. Chen Guohua is still at large. Yesterday, the Kangjiaqiao police station sent the two teachers, Yu and Zha, to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation and investigation, and at the same time, issued an arrest warrant for Principal Chen Guohua.

Vines and Perry Agreed to Forty Matches - To Be Held Across the United States From January to May Next Year - The Greatest Event in Tennis History

Berlin, November 20th (Reuters) It is reported that British tennis player Perry, who recently turned professional, will go to the United States in January next year to compete with Vines. The two have agreed to compete a total of forty times in major cities across the United States from January to May. This is the greatest event in tennis history. Their first match is scheduled for January 6th at Madison Square Garden in New York, followed by tours of Philadelphia, Boston, Chicago, Cleveland, and then Montreal, Vancouver, and other parts of Canada.

Commercial News

Yarn and Cotton - Squeezing in This Month is Becoming More Severe, Label Yarn Reaches a New High Price - 244 Yuan

China Cotton Company's Bulls Rely on Swaps to Loosen Slightly - Now Tianjin Gang's Purchase and Sale of Sole Good Yarn Pushes the Price Up by Another Two Yuan

The yarn market initially fell, but the bulls' intentions remained enthusiastic, and they were unwilling to give up their bull position. The squeeze on yarn this month became even deeper, and this month reached a new high price of 244 yuan. Following this, there was talk of resolving the labor unrest issue next Monday, and the gold industry gang came out in large numbers, as well as China Cotton Company's large amount of swaps, so the market appeared slightly looser. In fact, there should have been a reaction after consecutive sharp rises.

Label Yarn Rose Near, Fell Far

In the morning opening of the label yarn market, the near month was very strong due to the bulls' preparations to take delivery, and continued to rise. However, in the second session, Osaka's Three Products Yarn entered a high state, and the Qingdao Yarn Factory's labor unrest has not yet been resolved. Market prices rose session by session, and the Tianjin gang's purchase and sale of spot yarn were particularly strong, so the market became more bullish. As a result, the near month rose by 2.5 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price, and the far month rose by 5 jiao to 1.1 yuan. In the afternoon opening, retail investors who were squeezed out became firm and saw new highs again, but those who profited in the far month closed out and fell back. By the time of the three sessions closing, it was said that the yarn factory strike would be resolved soon, and a certain factory had released 20-count Jincheng Double Deer Double Happiness yarn, so the market squeezed and挫. As a result, each month fell by 6 jiao to 1.3 or 4 jiao compared to the morning closing price. It was found that 7,550 bales of Hexing were sold, 7,300 bales of Gengfeng, 1,050 bales of Changyu, 1,800 bales of Fengtai, 1,050 bales of Yuan Yi, 2,550 bales of Dachangcheng, 3,450 bales of Yichang, 4,600 bales of Run Kang, 4,000 bales of Xincheng, 1,500 bales of Yu Da, and 3,700 bales of Xingchang. 1,250 bales of Dafu were bought, 3,350 bales of Hengyi, 2,350 bales of Juxing, 6,150 bales of Mingde, 1,250 bales of Daqing, 3,450 bales of Sen Kang, 1,450 bales of Hengde, 4,800 bales of Renfeng, 5,350 bales of Changfeng, 4,500 bales of Rui Da, 1,950 bales of Taichang, and 3,000 bales of Tonghe. The highest and lowest prices of the day are listed on the left.

Yarn Sales of Over 2,000 Bales

Spot yarn sales are still smooth. It was found that the various gangs bought a total of 2,340 bales throughout the day, at a price of 2 yuan. The purchase amount of each gang is listed below: Inland 300, Guangdong 760, Tianjin 1,040, Shantou 10, Ningbo 10, Sichuan 60, Changsha 40, Yunnan 80, Nanjing 10, Jiangxi 30.

Labor Unrest Expected to Subside - Cotton Reaches a Good State - Each Month Rises Back by Three or Four Jiao

The cotton market turned firm, and the rising trend started slightly, because there was news that the labor unrest would be resolved next Monday, so the bulls were active and the shorts covered, and the market rebounded. Now the cotton mills need to be a little more active, and the inventory of cotton is strong, so there are still many people who are stubborn when prices rise.

Near Month Tongji扒空

In the morning opening of the label cotton market, the market was still calm because U.S. cotton rose and fell, up and down 1 to 6 pounds, and Indian cotton rose 2 rupees 25. After the second session, because the Tongji shorts covered their positions and the yarn market was good, the buying trend rose sharply, and the rising trend was urgent, with each month jumping 3 or 4 jiao. As a result, each month rose 4.5 to 5 jiao compared to the previous day's closing price. In the afternoon opening, the market said that the yarn factory labor unrest could be calmed down, so buyers were active and the situation was tighter. Tongji扒空 in the near month, and the far month was激動, each month rose by 2 jiao. Mi Meng

Silk and Tea: Foreign Firms Seem Satisfied with Silk

Yesterday, the foreign silk market was firm. Sales of native silk were relatively quiet, probably due to the recent unpredictable trends in the silk market. Currently, people are generally taking a wait-and-see approach, and foreign merchants seem quite content. Consequently, there were not many sales throughout the day. In the foreign market, Yokohama's near and distant futures each rose slightly by two or three yuan. New York's standard silk rose by half a cent to one cent. However, the holding price of Japanese silk 83 and 75 average grades rose by about three cents. Guangdong silk and Shanghai silk also rose by about two to three cents. In the Lyon silk market, holding prices for various items increased by one to two francs, it is said.

Oil and Hemp: Hemp Oil Rises with Raw Materials; New Huai Speed Goods Rise to Twenty-Six Yuan

The hemp oil market situation: Although the current "Geng" year's raw material production is still plentiful, the price at the source is high, making the supply source difficult to flourish. The new goods market opened at twenty yuan, but the arrivals are insufficient. Clocks are still acceptable, so the market immediately increased to twenty-five yuan. By the beginning of this month, there was a sudden interest from Ningbo, and retail sales on this street also showed activity, with six to seven hundred transactions. The price was raised again to twenty-five yuan and five jiao. In recent days, due to the continuous rise in raw materials, sellers' minds have become increasingly firm. With tight selling prices, the market rose to twenty-six yuan yesterday at a distance. 500 transactions were made, handled by that "Er Bang." According to the current supply source, the trend is expected to remain stable. After the old oil market was stirred by the inland gangs, although the color and taste of the goods have deteriorated, the route of that gang has not decreased slightly. After the market opened at twenty-two yuan, goods holders, seeing the lively sales, have been raising prices more and more vigorously. The market price has gradually increased. Last month, the Jinlan gang made moves on the sidelines. This month, the Hangzhou gang continues to take goods without stopping, with no less than two to three thousand "ting" transacted before and after, being snapped up completely. The market has risen to twenty-three yuan and six jiao. Currently, it is said that there is no inventory of the old goods available on the market, it is said.

"Without Air Defense, There is No National Defense"

— Yang Gonghuai

Children, do you know? Modern warfare is three-dimensional warfare, because the area of war is no longer limited to flat land or the sea, but has developed into the air. In future wars, the air force will be the most effective in combat. It can fly nimbly to the enemy's position without waiting for the mobilization of the army and navy, destroying their defensive works, disrupting their rear, and putting the enemy in a situation where attack and defense are both impossible. A country that can strengthen the combat power of its air force is certainly the best strategy for warfare; to consolidate national defense and resist foreign insults, it is also necessary to work hard on air defense!

The importance of air defense, I believe children already understand. So, how should we implement air defense?

From a passive perspective, measures such as implementing blackout regulations, organizing fire brigades, and enhancing anti-gas equipment are all very important. But from an active perspective, to defend against air raids without military aircraft with real strength to fight enemy aircraft, there will never be a huge, safe air defense cover to protect the country's industrial and commercial centers and national defense fortresses. Therefore, to actively defend against air raids, it is essential to strengthen the real strength of the air force; this is extremely clear. Our country is now at a crossroads of survival. In the Battle of Shanghai and the Battle of the Great Wall, our country suffered greatly from the threat and ravages of the enemy's air force due to the weakness of our air defense capabilities. This lesson we will never forget. In the future, we should mobilize the nation's manpower and financial resources to strengthen air defense in order to cope with future crises. Children! Please reflect on whether you have fulfilled your responsibilities, directly or indirectly, in terms of air defense.

I remember a foreign military expert once said, "Without air defense, there is no national defense." This sentence is indeed true, and I hope all the children will keep it in mind!

Random Tales of Children's Stories

— Yi Sheng

Xie Daoyun's Eulogy on Willow Catkins

Xie An rose to the position of Grand Tutor, and his family was known for its elegance. They often gathered together to discuss poetry and prose, so that the family was filled with the sounds of chanting and reciting. One day in winter, when it was snowing heavily, Xie An again summoned his children to gather around the stove to appreciate the snow and discuss literature. After a while, the snow fell even harder and faster. Xie An happily recited, "What does the swirling white snow resemble?" A nephew, whose nickname was Hu'er, blurted out, "It's like scattering salt in the air." A girl's voice interjected, "It's not as good as willow catkins rising in the wind!" Everyone looked over and saw that it was Xie An's niece, Xie Daoyun, who couldn't resist expressing her opinion and continued with this line. Xie An greatly praised and rejoiced. To this day, when praising women's literary talent, people often cite the story of Xie Daoyun's eulogy on willow catkins as a comparison.

Children from families who uphold poetry and propriety, and literary families, are cultivated by family education on a daily basis, so their literary cultivation surpasses that of children from ordinary families. However, a person's innate intelligence and the elegance or vulgarity of their mind are always related to talent and are difficult to force. The uncle set the topic, and the elder brother used scattering salt in the air to describe the flying snow, which could be considered approximate. The younger sister changed it to wind-blown willow catkins, which was not only natural—unlike the forced invention of scattering salt in the air—but also showed that the situation was more similar. Once this line was uttered, it was feared that no one else could compete with it! Such an elegant line of poetry coming from a young girl's mouth made it even more praiseworthy!

Song of Resistance Against the Enemy

— Lu Er Yu

Do not be discouraged,

Nor be afraid,

Do not look back,

Even if thorns catch your blue shirt.

You must walk!

You must advance!

Your road is endless,

Your responsibility is inexhaustible.

Thousands of eyes are watching you,

Thousands of fingers are pointing at you.

They watch your success, your failure,

You must first strengthen your courage!

Children!

More foolish than the camels in the desert,

Yet they do not refuse the hardships of this life!

A Proposal

— Zhuang Junjie, Sixth Grade, Nanyang Elementary School

Children! The current national situation has reached the final juncture of life and death! Look, the enemy has forcibly seized our four northeastern provinces and still wants to annex the whole of China. If everyone reads the newspaper every day, then you know the extent of the danger in North China, so I won't go into detail. Recently, the enemy has instigated a group of puppet bandits and traitors to harass our Suiyuan: and used their planes and cannons to attack Suiyuan desperately. However, the generals and soldiers defending Suiyuan are all very brave in resisting them; they are not afraid of hunger and cold, not afraid of sacrifice, and are determined to fulfill their duty; their spirit is so admirable!

However, Suiyuan is not Suiyuan of the Suiyuan soldiers, nor is it Suiyuan of the Suiyuan people, but Suiyuan of all Chinese people. Therefore, everyone has the responsibility to defend the territory. We children should not lag behind in loving our country and should also contribute some effort to fulfill our responsibility. Therefore, I have a proposal: to save the money that everyone would spend on sweets and toys in the next few days, collect it, and send it to the Shenbao to be forwarded to the warriors fighting the enemy on the front lines to buy clothes and rice. On the one hand, everyone should work hard to raise clothes, money, and goods from all sides and send them to the warriors as encouragement. I think "many grains of sand form a pagoda, many foxes' armpits make a fur coat," at least it will provide some help to the many fighters who are fighting the enemy! I hope the children will work together to support this great cause!

Why is it Cold on High Mountains?

— Shi Jiu

Min'er came home from school, and as usual, his father asked him what he had learned today. Min'er replied, "Today in science class, Mr. Lu told us that the closer we are to the sun, the hotter it is; so if there were no sun in the sky, humans and all living things would freeze to death."

His father smiled and said, "Then aren't high mountains closer to the sun? Why is there year-round snow on the mountain tops that doesn't melt? Also, in the summer, why do rich people insist on going to the mountains to escape the heat?"

Min'er thought for a moment and replied, "I don't know about that, but Mr. Lu wouldn't be wrong."

His father said, "Not knowing is not knowing, you are right; but you say that Mr. Lu is never wrong, then seeking knowledge should not be so careless. Regardless of whether what others say is right or wrong, we should study it carefully."

Min'er said, "Then, did Mr. Lu say something wrong?"

His father said, "No, what he said is very right. But we should think more when seeking knowledge. If Daddy were you, I would ask Mr. Lu the two questions I just raised."

Min'er listened and was filled with regret. His father comforted him and said, "Why doesn't the snow on the mountain tops melt year-round? Mr. Lu probably didn't have time to explain this. Let me explain it to you."

"Mountain tops are indeed closer to the sun. But we must know that to maintain body temperature, we must wear clothes. Similarly, to maintain the sun's temperature and prevent it from dissipating, there must be something important to wrap it up; there is no doubt about that. And this thing is increasingly lacking the higher you go from the ground. What do you think this is?"

Min'er said, "Since this thing cannot be seen, could it be air?"

His father smiled and said, "That's right. This air is like a blanket, wrapping the earth to preserve the temperature; and not just one blanket, but countless blankets wrapped around it, to prevent sunlight from escaping elsewhere. So, we not only need sunlight to give us heat, but also, once we have heat, we must rely on this thing, the 'blanket,' to wrap it up so that we don't feel cold. The higher you go from the ground, the thinner the air. The thinner the air, the easier it is for sunlight to dissipate. The easier it is for sunlight to dissipate, which is why the snow on high mountains doesn't melt year-round, even though the mountain tops are closer to the sun. Understanding this principle, then why rich people flock to the mountains to escape the summer heat is also self-evident."

Min'er listened and suddenly understood.

Starting from Eating Candied Chestnuts

— De Lin

Yesterday, around dusk, after finishing work, I was walking home from my business when I passed a fruit store. Beside the pedestrian path, they were frying candied chestnuts, and they had written "Tianjin Liangxiang" in glass-framed letters. I bought a few bags, and they were still warm and almost too hot to hold. After I got home, my seven-year-old cousin, who had finished school, was visiting. I opened two bags, and we peeled and ate the chestnuts together. This made me think of imperialist Japan and the good influence it constantly gave children in their daily lives, whether at home or at school.

For example, when an elementary school teacher talks to elementary school students about how candied chestnuts are the most delicious thing, then he will tell them that candied chestnuts are produced in Liangxiang, Tianjin. If we can seize North China, then we can eat as many as we want. Or when talking about oranges, the teacher will say: The oranges from Fujian, China, are the sweetest, even better than those produced in America. If we take down Fujian, then we can eat oranges endlessly. When talking about peaches, they must also say how sweet the peaches from Fenghua, China, are. If we fight to Fenghua, China, we can enjoy them without end. From this point, we can see the importance that Japanese imperialism places on children's education. In every action and contact of children, and in their daily lives, they are constantly stirring up their patriotism and their interest in aggression, while also arousing their sense of responsibility to the nation. This is something we should pay attention to.

Because eating candied chestnuts made me think of the cultivation of children's daily lives by Japanese imperialism, but in China, we should also give children some enlightenment of patriotic thought. For example, when eating candied chestnuts, we can also tell them that Liangxiang, Tianjin, the place where candied chestnuts are produced, is about to be taken by the enemy. We should find a way to reclaim it. In this way, at least we can arouse their fragile little minds to understand how serious the national crisis is and how imperialist the aggression is, so that when they grow up and step into society, they can take on the responsibility of serving the country and recovering lost territories.

Physical Little Knowledge

— Yan Maode

Why do the bristles of a writing brush spread out in all directions in water and then gather into a bundle when taken out of the water?

When washing a writing brush, the bristles suddenly spread out in all directions, and then gather into a bundle when taken out of the water. Children! Do you have such questions when washing brushes? Originally, when the brush is in water, each molecule has an adhesive force with the brush, so it spreads out in all directions. When it leaves the water and faces outwards, because water has surface tension, it can make the brush gather into a bundle.

Why does a stick appear bent when inserted into water?

A stick appears bent when inserted into water. This is due to the refraction of light. Refraction occurs when light passes through two objects of different densities. When light enters the water from the air, it appears farther from the surface of the water than its actual path. Conversely, when it emerges from the water into the air, it appears closer to the surface of the water than its actual path, so it looks like it has been refracted.

Children! When you take a stick and insert it into a place with water, you can tell that what I am saying is true.

Children's Creation

Chrysanthemum

— Wu Pinxian, Fifth Grade, Shanghai Zhiben Elementary School

In our school, there is a small garden. Inside the garden, there is a row of fences. Beside the fences, there are dozens of chrysanthemums. They have green and messy leaves, looking like a pile of messy green grass. In the garden, besides chrysanthemums, there are also many famous flowers. From spring to autumn, they bloom one after another. After class, the students all go to admire the famous flowers, and no one even glances at the chrysanthemums.

As autumn deepens, the chrysanthemums must develop their path of life. Although the cold northwest wind blows and thick frost covers them, the chrysanthemums are not overwhelmed by the wind and frost. They can actually invigorate their spirits and fight against the violent wind and frost. As a result, the wind and frost lose their violence, and the chrysanthemums bloom proudly.

At this time, the periwinkles, roses, and other flowers in the enclosure have either shed their flowers and leaves, or their branches and trunks are standing bare. Only the chrysanthemums beside the fences, blooming in red, white, yellow, purple, and all sorts of colors, are incomparably beautiful, and the students all come to admire the chrysanthemums.

I think: The chrysanthemum's results today come from fighting through the severe cold. Looking at our China, which is constantly being invaded by imperialism, we four hundred million compatriots must protect our country and ensure the survival of our nation. We should invigorate our spirits, work together with one heart, and point our guns at the outside. If our country wants to be powerful in the world, there is no other way but to resist and fight.

The Talking Oil Lamp

— Reply to Wang Ziqiang of Guangzhou

Dear Ziqiang,

We have received your letter. Your account of the camping situation in Shipai is very detailed and also very interesting. We are very willing to accept many of your suggestions for this mailbox. Within the realm of possibility, we are willing to do our best to improve.

The questions you have raised are indeed worthy of attention. When practicing light signals at night, you naturally have to use a flashlight. But it also has its drawbacks. First, it is uneconomical, and second, there is no way to use it once the battery is used up. After detailed discussion, we think there are some remedial methods, and we are going to tell you here a more practical method.

Don't you take tents with you when you go out camping? Also, don't you have lights on your bicycle team? This is a very good communication light. Kerosene can be bought anywhere, unlike batteries, which can only be bought in more prosperous places, and the price of kerosene is much cheaper than batteries! Therefore, we think that oil lamps can be used to replace them when practicing light signals.

You can take a few pieces of wood and nail them into a lidded wooden box. Dig a round hole in the front of the wooden box, and then nail a movable wooden board on the upper end of the hole, and engrave a handle on it. Then put the lighted oil lamp in the box, point the light at the hole, and close the box. This is done. You only need to move the handle up and down by hand, and the wooden board in front of the box will move up and down accordingly. Then, the longer the time the wooden board is lifted, the longer the time the light shines out, and the light will not be seen when the wooden board covers the hole. In this way, you can use the duration and number of exposures to represent various signs of telegraphy, and the other party will clearly receive the information you send.

Do you think our method can be used? Please, wish you progress!

— Written by Jiang Zhongyu

(1) Before going to bed, Min'er read a picture book of undersea animals. (2) In the middle of the night, he had a dream. (3) He sailed a small boat on the sea. (4) Suddenly, a storm rose on the sea. (5) Min'er's boat was overturned by the wind. (6) Min'er sank into the water.

The Mourning of the Northeast Boy Scouts after the Completion of the National Boy Scout Review

— Hong Fu transcription

The second national Boy Scout review has already closed on October 11! The Boy Scouts of each unit have certainly happily returned home! But our respectable and lovely Boy Scouts from the four provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe are very moved. Before the Boy Scouts from all over left the camp, they gave a very sad farewell on the camp's broadcasting station, reporting on the current situation of the children in the Northeast. Now I will introduce this valuable farewell to the children!

Dear children: You saw the Boy Scouts from the four northeastern provinces also came to participate in this national review and camping, and everyone felt very excited and expressed endless joy. When we first arrived at the camp, we judged that everyone's hearts were like this based on the various hints you gave us. Today, in the review field, everyone gave us an extraordinary welcome, which further confirmed that our prediction was correct. We cannot repay your sympathy and welcome, only shed a few tears, increase a few points of shared hatred, and increase a few points of self-confidence in the work of revitalizing the nation and recovering lost land. When the lost land is recovered, everyone will give us the same sympathy and assistance. We decided to keep the units of the four northeastern provinces in this great review and great camping. We received this news very late. Due to the limited time and the difficulty of preparation, very few people participated, which looked very deserted, adding a lot of sadness to everyone. We are very sorry for this, but after this review is over, we will continue to work hard and work harder to thank everyone for their warm welcome.

We have brought some news from the children living in the Northeast these days. I want to report to you. Everyone must be very willing to listen to it. What is their living situation like? ! ! The director of every school is a person of a certain country, and there are many more people of a certain country as teachers, and some schools even have principals who are from that country! ! ! In that kind of environment, not only can they not read the Three Principles of the People, they cannot read Chinese history, they cannot read Chinese geography, and even books related to the spirit of martial arts have become forbidden books! ! ! Of course, they have no chance to receive Boy Scout training or to participate in large reviews and camps. What do they do? ! ? Let me give you an example of a meeting! The first thing is to visit Yuying, which is to pay the highest respect to the pseudo-emperor Pu Ni. The second thing is to read the edict, which is the edict issued by the pseudo-emperor Pu Ni. The third thing is to sing the pseudo-national anthem. The fourth thing is to worship Gaocheng from afar, which is to pay homage to the place where the pseudo-emperor Pu Ni lives. Everyone, think about it, are they willing to do these things? ! Of course, they are unwilling, but in that kind of environment, they have to do it that way. How painful they are spiritually, and whether their life or property is guaranteed in the slightest. The pain in other aspects is even more difficult to express in words. Everyone heard this news, you must be more active and more sympathetic; or want to immediately save the children in the Northeast who are in deep water. Now I agree with everyone, and follow the instructions of the General Assembly, to intensify training and strive for self-cultivation in the various rules given to us, and under the guidance of the Chairman, to complete our mission. For the work of revitalizing the nation, we are willing to follow after you all and work together. For the work of recovering the lost land in the Northeast, we are willing to stand on the front line and fight to the death with the powerful forces. Finally, thank you all and wish you all health and unlimited prospects.

Filial Piety (5)

— Hai

Because the passport Basi Ke Fei carried stated that she was the daughter of an army colonel, she received a great deal of attention from lower-ranking officials along the way. The instances where she received favorable treatment were too numerous to count, while cases of rejection or neglect were relatively few. Later, she would say to people, "People always think that my long journey was very dangerous because they only heard me talk about various adventures, and didn't pay attention to the times I received preferential treatment."

There was one instance where she had a great fright. She knocked on many doors in a village, asking for lodging for the night, but was refused by everyone. However, an old man, after initially refusing her, suddenly ran up and called her back. She did not like his face very much, but she had no other choice and had to turn around and go with him. His wife had just as unpleasant a face. As soon as they entered the small house, they bolted the door with a thick iron bolt. A few pieces of oak were burning in a hole in the wall. Basi Ke Fei, in the faint light of the fire, saw that the old couple looked very troubled, and they immediately asked her where she came from.

Basi Ke Fei replied, "From Yiji Village. I'm going to St. Petersburg." The two of them asked, "Do you have a lot of money with you?" "Now I only have eighty copper kopeks left," Basi Ke Fei answered. She secretly rejoiced in her heart that she only had this little money left.

The old woman shouted, "That's a lie! People can't travel such a long distance without money."

Although she tried her best to explain that she really only had that much money, they still didn't believe her, which made her both frightened and angry, and she couldn't help but shed tears. Finally, they gave her a few sweet potatoes to eat and told her to lie down on a large brick stove, because the surface of the stove was very wide and flat. Poor Russians often used it as a bed. She took off her coat and put it aside, along with her purse and luggage bag, thinking that there was only a small amount of money in the purse, and that it would not lead to murder for money. She then prayed very sincerely and lay down. After a while, they thought she was asleep and began to whisper to each other.

"She must have more money, she must have banknotes."

The old woman quickly said, "I saw a chain around her neck with a small bag hanging on it, her money must be hidden there."

They lowered their voices even more and said, "No one saw her come to our house, no one knows she's still in this village."

Before long, Basi Ke Fei was shocked to see the old woman climbing onto the stove. She hurriedly explained that she really had no money and begged for her life, but the old woman did not answer, only pulled the bag from her neck, and felt all over her clothes, and took off her boots, and pried open her hands, while the old man held a lamp and shone it to the side; but after searching for a while, they saw that there was only a passport in the bag, and nothing else, so they left her and went to sleep.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Commentary

The Shanghai Citizens Unite to Donate 100,000 Woolen Sweaters to Support Suiyuan!

— Huang Shuwen

The citizens of Shanghai have always been enthusiastic in supporting and assisting the self-defense war to maintain the survival of the nation and the people. This has been fully demonstrated in the experiences of the Northeast Volunteer Army's resistance, etc. Recently, although foreign aggression has become more and more urgent, the patriotic sentiments of people from all walks of life have become increasingly high. Suiyuan is the first line of our national defense, no, it is the last line of our national defense, and it is the last barrier in the Central Plains of our country after the fall of the four northeastern provinces and the occurrence of the Hebei-Chahar issue. This Suiyuan defense war, which is related to the final survival of the country, has finally opened the prelude to the war after many days of brewing. Despite the friendly nations' declarations that it was a conflict between the Chinese regular army and local bandits, and despite the traitors' attempts to cover it up, saying that the bandits were not worth worrying about; discerning people all understand the background and intentions of the bandit-puppet invasion of Suiyuan, and are also wary of the importance of the gains and losses of the Suiyuan defense. Moreover, General Fu Zuoyi and the spirit of his subordinates' courageous resistance and the enthusiasm of loyalty to defend the country are no less than those of the past anti-enemy generals. No wonder that as soon as the war began, the "Aid Suiyuan Movement" in North China and other places sprang up like mushrooms, reaching its peak. The advocacy of Shanghai's various groups to organize the Suiyuan Army Support Association is naturally an urgent need. Curtailing food and using it to provide material assistance has already been advocated and begun, but the movement to donate cold clothes by reducing clothing has not yet been noticed. From the reports of those who went to the front to comfort the soldiers, we already know that the soldiers defending the border in the bitter cold of early winter need cold clothes the most, but I believe that buying clothes with donated money is not as economical and convenient as directly donating old clothes, and donating woolen sweaters among old clothes is the most suitable. My reasons are as follows:

(1) The sacrifice of donating old clothes is smaller than donating money, especially in the minds of the masses, they feel that this is a benevolent and inexpensive thing, so the results will be more enthusiastic and considerable.

(2) It is necessary to remit money to Suiyuan first, and then remit it to cities or inland to purchase military clothing, then the remittance fee and time have already suffered two losses.

(3) The cost of purchasing new cotton clothes is relatively large. In the current market where yarn and flowers are rising and there are shortages everywhere, whether there can be sufficient supply is still a question. Even if there is, the price controlled by foreign merchants will be even higher, so it is better to donate surplus old clothes, which is in line with economic principles.

(4) Donating clothes to the army is not like donating to refugees, where you can ignore the style and length, and only take warmth, and the army's clothing should be neat and light, in order to strengthen the military prestige and facilitate combat, so cotton robes and long clothes are not suitable, but woolen sweaters or woolen underwear can be worn inside the military uniform, which is more suitable.

(5) China's woolen industry is currently very developed, and its products are cheap and of good quality. When citizens replenish new clothes, they can promote industry and commerce. Furthermore, few women are engaged in production, and it is difficult to have surplus money to donate, so inspecting and sending old woolen sweaters and rushing to make new woolen sweaters will be one of the practical work of women saving the country.

As for the donation method, it should of course be initiated and planned by the "Suiyuan Army Support Association" organized by various circles, in order to achieve uniform and universal results. Now I would like to contribute some opinions based on the points that the author has thought of:

(1) The ideal method is to take the family as a unit, with each family donating at least one piece. Woolen sweaters are not as easy to remit or send in person as money, so after the date of announcement, the support association should send personnel to collect them door-to-door by truck.

(2) Before the collection, there should be about ten days of newspaper publicity and broadcast publicity to give citizens sufficient preparation: those who already have two or more pieces should check and store the older ones in advance, and those who only have one piece should immediately purchase and weave new clothes for replacement.

(3) The clothing collection personnel should bring formal receipts in advance, and a slip should be issued for each piece at any time. Only a name and house number need to be filled in. Prepare a stamp for "Shanghai Supporting Suiyuan Woolen Sweater" for each person and stamp it on the clothes on the spot to prove that the clothes will not be stolen, sold, or lost.

(4) If, during the first door-to-door solicitation, some people are willing to donate but cannot rush to make them in time, or have not seen the publicity beforehand, the clothing collection personnel should record the house number and collect the names of the places where donations have not been made after one week.

(5) The solicitation is mainly for woolen sweaters, and other short clothes that are suitable for military use can also be collected, but the word "Other" should be noted on the receipt to distinguish and facilitate statistics.

(6) In order to show credibility, it may be necessary to announce the results. The method is: put a piece of cloth on each lane, only fill in "Several pieces at No. 1 in this lane, several pieces at No. 2, ... Total number of pieces", etc., and the newspaper publishes the total results only in units of lanes, that is, several pieces in a certain lane on a certain road, without having to announce the official title, in order to save advertising space, and it is very convenient for citizens to check and compare. If there is any discrepancy, they can question and correct it at any time.

The above-mentioned methods are some points that I have thought of based on the special nature of donating clothes. As for the detailed methods, I hope that all circles will study and discuss them. Among them, there is a very obvious feature, that is, one receipt for each donated clothing item, unlike money receipts, which are more difficult to calculate and check, so it can reduce or prevent fraud and increase the faith of citizens. Also, old clothes are only for wearing, unlike money that can be used for other purposes, and stamping on the clothes can prevent theft, exchange, and loss. In the past, some citizens of Shanghai groundlessly suspected the use of donations to support Ma, which caused many enthusiastic groups and organizations that collected donations on behalf of others to suffer a lot of injustice. It can be seen that this method should be properly used to increase effectiveness.

If the above opinions are supported by all circles and put into practice, then calculating based on Shanghai's population of more than 3 million, with an average of one woolen sweater donated by five people per family, there should be as many as 600,000 pieces. Shanghai is originally a place where people value clothing regardless of wealth or poverty. Even if those who are too poor to afford woolen sweaters are excluded, at least 100,000 pieces is not a problem. These 100,000 woolen sweaters can immediately warm the hearts of 100,000 soldiers who are bitterly guarding the border, and at the same time save hundreds of thousands of dollars that should be used to purchase cotton clothes, which can be used to supply military equipment and provisions. The effect of this, whether in terms of enriching national defense strength or as a spiritual encouragement, cannot be measured in miles. The author hopes with all his heart that all circles of citizens in Shanghai, especially the women's circle, will unite to support and promote it, so as to add a great new force to the national defense support! (The manuscript fee will be transferred to the "Suiyuan Frontline Soldiers Comfort Money" sponsored by this newspaper.)
