Supporting Suiyuan and Aiding Spanish Women and Children

— Ji Cong

The Spanish masses, for the sake of freedom and peace, have been fighting bloody battles for several months with the rebel army that colluded with foreign aggressors. During this period, the rebel leader, because he was willing to be a slave to Hitler and Mussolini, and willing to secretly offer his country's land and rights to the invading countries, obtained a large number of poisonous gases, aircraft, artillery, and various latest killing weapons from Germany and Italy to brutally kill the domestic people who protect the republic and love peace, and even ordinary women and children. People with a sense of justice all over the world are very angry about this situation; they have given the legitimate government and the masses of the people of Spain active assistance from all aspects, and some have even run to Madrid to participate in the frontline and fight hand-to-hand with the rebel army, making the invaders frightened! Because our country is far away from Spain, although there has been no active assistance to the resistance of the people of that country in the past, recently Ms. Soong Ching Ling and others have initiated the assistance to Spanish women and children, declaring and calling on women and compatriots across the country to provide assistance to the Spanish government and people, and hoping that our country's women will follow the spirit of Western women sacrificing for the country and unite to strive for national independence. This situation, as it is currently manifested, not only has not lost its timeliness in the slightest, but also has greater significance.

We are a weak and small nation that is being invaded and oppressed. All humans who are being invaded and oppressed in the world, as well as forces that sympathize with the oppressed, are our friendly forces; conversely, all invaders and oppressors are our enemies. Therefore, when any group of oppressed and invaded people in any part of the world is attacked, we should strive to help, just as the invaded people all over the world should help us when we encounter invasion: moreover, only when we and the friendly forces all over the world unite to help each other can everyone be liberated. The legitimate government of Spain and its freedom- and peace-loving masses have been cruelly attacked by the invading forces. If we do not actively provide assistance, the invaders will win, and the invading forces all over the world will inevitably expand greatly, making our liberation encounter greater difficulties. Now, the cruel war in Spain is at a critical juncture, and at the same time, our direct enemies are using force to seize our Suiyuan and North China. Objectively, our fate is the same as that of the people of the West, and everyone's current urgent task of resisting aggression and striving for independence and freedom is also the same; therefore, our current assistance to Spain is actually also assisting ourselves.

Now, the people of our country are actively supporting and assisting the heroic resistance of the Suiyuan soldiers; at the same time, there has been a warm expression of sympathy for the Spanish people's bloody battle with the invading forces: this fully proves that the eyes of the people of our country are still clear, the blood is still boiling, they can still recognize the current enemy, and they still have the greatest determination to actively resist the enemy. However, so far, our assistance to the Suiyuan anti-enemy soldiers is only monetary donations and spiritual encouragement, and we have not resolved to implement it by going to the frontline to fight with the soldiers there; and the current military force on the frontline is extremely limited, and the national military force has not yet prepared a general mobilization to deal with the enemy's new offensive; this is of course very insufficient. We know that the bandit army attacking Suiyuan is not an ordinary bandit, but a vanguard bought by the invaders. They have artillery, airplanes, and various new types of weapons, and the army and military supplies are constantly increasing, and the invading forces are mixed in with them; although my Suiyuan soldiers are brave, how can they resist such an invading force for a long time if they are not actively assisted by military force? It is really pitiful to say that we only see the enemy's planes bombing our positions in the newspaper, but we have not seen our own planes attacking the enemy. Where have our many planes gone! At the same time, there are still problems with the past anti-enemy strategy, that is, only trying to conserve, not to attack; this kind of resistance is tantamount to helping the enemy preserve its position and predetermining to offer the final victory to the enemy. In the future, we should completely reverse this method, and we should use the general mobilization of the whole country, with careful and complete preparation, with the greatest determination and courage, to attack section by section from Shangdu until we completely recover the lost land. Only in this way can we eliminate the invaders' ambition, obtain the thorough liberation of the Chinese nation, and achieve true peace in East Asia.

The liberation of the oppressed Chinese nation, and the loss of power by some of the invaders, will inevitably deal the greatest blow to the invading forces of the entire world, and the Spanish people and the world's masses who are being ravaged by the invading forces will also be easier to be liberated. Therefore, our national mobilization to resist the enemy by force is also to aid Spain and to aid the invaded and oppressed people of the world. Currently, aiding Suiyuan and Spain are both our major tasks.

Overseas Correspondence Network

The World's Tallest Building

— Junsheng

New York Correspondence

If you take a boat to New York, when the boat is about to reach this metropolis, look up and you can see a tall building that cannot be seen anywhere else in the world. It stands in the midst of all the large and small buildings in New York City, just like a Christmas candle standing among many fruits, displaying itself very specially. If you want to walk under it and look up, you will lose your hat, open your eyes wide, and break your neck, and it will be difficult to see its top floor clearly. This building is New York's tallest building, the Empire State Building.

The Eiffel Tower in Paris is the tallest tower in the world, with a height of nearly a thousand feet, which is certainly quite surprising. But the Empire State Building is three hundred feet taller than that tower! From the street to the top floor, it is one thousand two hundred and forty-eight feet high; if you are happy to calculate using Chinese feet, you will get an even more amazing number. It actually has eighty-six floors, but on top of that there is a two-hundred-foot-high tower from the eighty-seventh to the one hundred and second floors, where giant airships are moored in the air.

The fastest wind speed in the United States is one hundred and eighty-six miles per hour. A building as tall as the Empire State Building would be extremely dangerous if it were not well designed. On this point, Mr. Balkan, the consulting engineer of the construction company that built it, also paid special attention; he adopted a unique design and used a safe method to make such a large wind force helpless against such a tall building. It is worth mentioning here that the top of the building is equipped with a Gothic-style steel arch, on which there is equipment for tethering airships. In the evening, you can see a star-like red light flashing on the top of the tower tethering the airship, which is the identification mark for nighttime flight. At the same time, there are four pillars in the place where the airship is attacked, all made of steel; they all run through this building and deep into the ground thirty-three feet, standing on the foundation of the rock. Therefore, even if the tethered airship is blown by the wind, it will not have much impact on the overall building.

How much material does it take to consume such a tall building? We certainly have no way to estimate. However, according to the person in charge of the construction company that contracted to build it, there are 58,000 tons of iron alone; of which, the four central columns alone weigh 10 million pounds, or 5,000 tons. I'm afraid you haven't heard of this kind of situation.

The Empire State Building has sixty-two special express elevators, which automatically rise and fall and stop according to signals. Their speed is roughly one thousand two hundred feet per minute, so it only takes a little more than a minute to rush from the first floor to the top one hundred and second floor. It is said that the speed of the elevators here can exceed this, but because New York's laws limit the speed of elevators to a maximum of one thousand two hundred feet per minute, the elevators here can only be opened to this speed.

There is an observation deck on the eighty-sixth floor. If you want to climb this observation deck, you should change to another elevator on the eightieth floor; if you want to go to the place where the airship is tethered on the top, you must change machines from here. There is a room there that can accommodate fifty people, which is the highest house in New York, no, maybe the highest house in the world.

This spring, the elevator employees in New York City had a major strike, and many people living in tall buildings felt great difficulties; especially those noble women who wore high-heeled leather shoes that were two or three inches high, who had always walked less, and had never climbed high slopes, so when the agile elevator suddenly became a dead object, it was really like suffering extremely cruel torture for them to go up and down automatically in houses hundreds or even thousands of feet high! That situation made us believe that what Sinclair described in "The Peaceful World" was not entirely fantasy. (Note) At this time, the sixty-two elevators in New York's tallest building, more than 1,200 feet high, were also motionless. The gentlemen and wealthy people who usually lived in this highest house, overlooking New York, looking out over America, and eyeing the globe, could only stand helplessly on the lower floors of that building, looking up at the roof that reached into the clouds, and sighing in vain. However, there were some idle and curious people in the world who took this opportunity to climb this more than 1,000-foot-high building with a stopwatch. It is said that it was quite fun at the beginning, but when they reached the sixty-eighth floor, they had no energy to go up anymore: looking at their watch, more than three and a half hours had passed since they started climbing. At the same time, it was also said that at the beginning, they averaged one floor per minute, but later they gradually became tired. When they reached the ninetieth floor, they felt sore feet and aching waists, and they wanted to rest very much; as a result, they only went up to the sixty-eighth floor and retreated dejectedly.

According to statistics, the electricity required by the Empire State Building is 3,500 kilowatts, which is equivalent to the needs of a large city with a population of 400,000. If the iron used in it is gathered together, it can be cast into a double-track railway five hundred miles long between New York and Mendel. At the same time, the length of the electric wires and telephone wires used in it is 2 million feet, which can circle the earth twice. As for all the arrangements inside and the consumption of the masters living in it, it is even more difficult to count. However, on the streets of New York, and in the country of America, there are many unemployed people wandering around, and their families not only have no elevators and telephones, no beautiful furniture, but also no bread and daily necessities!

As for the owner of this building, it is the famous American politician Al Smith. He used to be the governor of New York and twice the Democratic presidential candidate. But in the 1928 American presidential election, he was defeated by the Republican Party, and since then he has left politics and entered the business world, joining hands with the American tycoon DuPont to buy the Waldorf-Astoria Hotel, which is known as the boundary mark of New York, for 13.5 million US dollars, and then he worked hard to plan and build this world's first building.

Every day from 8:00 AM to midnight, this tallest building is open to the public; at the same time, a register is also prepared at the top for officials, dignitaries, and tycoons from all over the world to leave their names, and the owner of the building, Al Smith, is also very happy to receive these distinguished guests. As for the poor and lowly people, they are of course not destined to be associated with this building.

(Note) Sinclair's novel "The Peaceful World" once described the difficulties of noble women walking in dozens of floors high buildings during a workers' strike in imagination, which made people sigh and marvel. A Chinese translation of this work by "Zhao Zhao She" was available a few years ago, but it seems that it cannot be bought now.

Small Monographs

Research on Population in Chinese History

— Hao Gu

When people mention China's population, they immediately say 400 million, but how many are there actually? Leaving aside historical populations, let's just talk about the present. The so-called 400 million is still an estimate from the Daoguang twenty-second year of the Qing Dynasty, and it was only a rough estimate by Westerners residing in China at the time. It definitely cannot be said to be an accurate statistic. Not to mention then, it is still the same now. Chinese government agencies and social scholars cannot give a definite figure on this issue. As for China's history, whether it is official history, unofficial history, popular novels, or historical anecdotes, all record the population figures of various dynasties and states, but it goes without saying that these are even further from the actual numbers. However, in our spare time from reading history, we collect them at any time, make a systematic summary, and analyze them. Although we cannot say that this will reveal the real changes in the population of past dynasties in China, it can at least prove the impact of turmoil and prosperity on population, and at the same time, it can provide some interesting material for those who specialize in the study of social history and economic history.

Since Malthus's "Essay on the Principle of Population" was published, everyone has regarded the law that population increases in geometric progression as an indisputable truth. They even attribute the struggles between groups of people, between countries, and between races, the development or stagnation of the economy, and the rise or fall of politics to the population principle. If this is the case, then the stagnation of the population and the failure to increase must be explained by the population itself, and the development and evolution of society must also be determined by the population law. But why has the population of various countries in the world increased dramatically in the last two centuries, while it has stagnated for thousands of years in ancient and medieval times? It can be seen that explaining population with population cannot yield an answer. The rapid population growth in modern Western Europe is due to the rapid development of production in Western Europe. The development of industry and commerce means that economic power is sufficient to support a larger population, and it also requires a large population to engage in production, so the population also increases. Conversely, in ancient and medieval times, the world's economy remained in a state of slave economy and feudal economy, with only scattered, small-scale, and slow production, so it could not support a large population, and therefore the population did not increase. It can be seen that the population problem is determined by the economy rather than the economy being determined by the population. With this basic principle in mind, we can study the population problem in Chinese history.

The books we are based on are mainly the "San Tong Kao," namely, the "Wenxian Tong Kao," the "Huangchao Tong Kao," and the "Xu Tong Kao." In addition, we also refer to the official histories of various dynasties, such as the "Shi Ji" and the "Han Shu." Furthermore, we are only studying to get an overview, so we especially highlight the population during the extremely important transitional periods of dynasties; as for population statistics for each dynasty and each year, they are too cumbersome and unimportant, and are mostly omitted. Finally, because the dynasties were not completely unified politically, we had to add up the simultaneous records of various states when compiling statistics, without considering the numbers of each state. There were also many times when many states lacked population statistics altogether. This can only be found in miscellaneous histories and the documents of political theorists at the time, but this is even more of a rough number. Moreover, the further back in time we go, the more inaccurate the numbers are, because we cannot have as much reference material to corroborate them as we do when studying modern times. Now, let's try to make a statistic based on the San Tong Kao:

In the era of Xia Yu, the number of households is unknown, but the population was said to be more than 13.5 million. In the early Zhou Dynasty, it was more than 13.7 million. The difference between the two dynasties is not large, but the Shang Dynasty between the two dynasties is nowhere to be found. When the Zhou Dynasty moved east, it was 11.9 million. The end of the Zhou Dynasty and the beginning of the Han Dynasty are both unknown. From the decrease in population when the Zhou Dynasty moved east, it can be seen that the chaos of the Eastern Zhou Dynasty and the invasion of the Quanrong were very related. Unfortunately, the "San Tong Kao" does not record the Warring States period, the Chu-Han contention, and the early Han Dynasty, but the general idea can be inferred from the documents of Su Qin and Zhang Yi lobbying the six states, although they are somewhat exaggerated. Su Qin said that Yan, Zhao, Han, and Qi all had hundreds of thousands of armored soldiers, and Chu had millions. Zhang Yi said that Qin had millions of soldiers. The number of soldiers at the time can also be verified by the number of chariots. Su Qin said that Qi, Chu, and Zhao each had 1,000 chariots; Yan had 600; Wei had 600 chariots and 5,000 riders; and Qin had 1,000 chariots and 10,000 riders. If each chariot and 10 riders were matched with 1,000 soldiers, then the total number of soldiers in the seven states would be 7 million. According to Su Qin, "Linzi has 70,000 households, with three men in each household, then Linzi can have 210,000 soldiers." Based on this, the population of the seven states should be more than 2 million households. If each household is counted as "eight people, then 20 million people can be obtained. But there are still many small states, such as Song, Wei, and Zhongshan, that have not been included, so the population of the Warring States period may have been 20 to 30 million. People often think that during the Warring States period, due to years of war, the population must have gradually decreased. But in fact, the primitive industrial and commercial economy was very developed at that time, as can be seen from Shang Yang's abolition of the well-field system and opening up the fields. At that time, the culture of the scholars was also very brilliant. The economic development created strong countries, and the population also increased compared to before. However, we must also note that the Chinese territory at this time was already larger than that of the Xia and Zhou dynasties.

If people who have studied social history know that in the early stages of slave society, because large numbers of slaves were used for production, not only agriculture was improved, but also primitive industry and commerce were greatly active. The Western Han Dynasty was a typical stage of slave society in Chinese history, and it was a period of prosperity for slave society. For example, the wealth of Emperor Wen and Emperor Jing of the Han Dynasty, and Deng Tong, who became a wealthy man by operating a tenth of the profits with favor. Because of economic development, the population number also increased greatly. At the end of the Western Han Dynasty, before Wang Mang, the number of households was more than 12 million, and the population was 60 million. Later, during the time of Emperor Guangwu of the Han Dynasty, the population suddenly decreased. According to historical facts, this era was an era of peasant rebellions. Liu Xiu (Emperor Guangwu) was also born as a peasant, and followed the vagrant proletarians in rebelling against the government. At that time, slave society had developed to the point of saturation and could no longer be progressive. The slave economic system had also become corrupt at this time, and it could not be remedied by itself, so the peasants were forced to rebel. At this time, the population also decreased sharply, with only more than 4.2 million households and a population of more than 20 million.

However, the resistance of slaves could not overthrow the political system of slave society, and they never had a way out. As a result of the rebellion, the rulers suppressed them and restored the original state. But at this time, the slave system was also on its last breath, half-paralyzed, and could no longer develop. Therefore, the population at that time could never exceed its prosperous period. At the end of the Eastern Han Dynasty, there were more than 16 million households and a population of 50 million. The population was the smallest during the Three Kingdoms period, with only more than 7 million. But this is absolutely incorrect. Naturally, the social turmoil, such as the disturbance of the peasants (Yellow Turban rebels), and the wars between states had an impact, but it could never have dropped from the previous 50 million to more than 70 percent. However, from this drastic reduction, it can also be seen that the society at that time could no longer support itself as it was. If there was no external force involved, it would die on its own. Like the Roman Empire in Western Europe, in its later period, there would inevitably be invasions by foreign tribes to infiltrate its vitality, such as the Germanic people. China was the same. From the Western Jin Dynasty onwards, it was the Five Barbarians' Rebellion. Society changed as a result, from a slave society to another society (social historians in China do not have a consistent judgment on this society. Some say it was a feudal society, and some say it was a transitional society, the former like Wang Yichang, the latter like Tao Xisheng). From then until the Opium War of the Manchu Qing Dynasty, it was the same. Therefore, the population of the later dynasties, although there were increases and decreases, was roughly the same, and the feudal economy was only a small-scale peasant economy, which could not support the lives of many people. Now, let's list the population of the later dynasties as follows:

At the end of the Northern and Southern Dynasties, it was more than 11 million. During the peak of the Sui Dynasty, it was more than 46 million. It is unknown during the time of Emperor Taizong of the Tang Dynasty, but there were only 8 million households. During the Tianbao years of Emperor Xuanzong of the Tang Dynasty, it was 52 million. During the time of Emperor Taizu of the Song Dynasty, it was 20 million. During the time of Emperor Gaozong of the Southern Song Dynasty, it was 19 million (excluding Jin), while the population of Jin was more than 20 million. At the beginning of the Yuan Dynasty, it was 58 million, and it is unknown at the end of the Yuan Dynasty. During the time of Emperor Chengzu of the Ming Dynasty, it was more than 66 million, and there was not much change after that. By the Qing Dynasty, the population decreased instead. In the eighteenth year of Shunzhi, it was 21 million, and in the fiftieth year of Kangxi, it was 24 million. But in the fourteenth year of Qianlong, it changed to 177 million, and by the forty-eighth year of Qianlong, it suddenly increased to 284 million.

It is thought that there were not many errors in the population after the Northern and Southern Dynasties and before the Qing Dynasty, and the relationship is also small. The population at the beginning of the Qing Dynasty must be inaccurate, and the population in the early years of Qianlong may be correct, but it suddenly increased to more than 100 million in just thirty years. Although this can be explained by the conquest of Xinjiang and the opening up of territory, it cannot be completely believed. However, in any case, we can also see that the social economy of China by the time of Qianlong had reached the beginning of the collapse of the feudal economy and the beginning of industrial capital economy. In addition, trade with overseas countries stimulated the development of domestic commerce, so it had the economic power to support a large population, and it also needed this large population.

In the last hundred years, the population has certainly been increasing day by day. If the four northeastern provinces and the frontier areas of Mongolia and Tibet are included, it may be no less than 400 million people. But in recent years, on the one hand, it has encountered the world economic panic. Capitalism has run into obstacles in the imperialist countries, not to mention our semi-colony, which is the end of its dumping. The economy has stagnated, and the population will also stagnate. What's more, it has been compounded by years of droughts and floods, as well as the encroachment of strong neighbors? So it is possible that the current population has decreased to 300 million.

Outlying Post Office Agency

Japanese Capital's Advance into Eastern Hebei

— Chen Shen

Hebei Tongxian Correspondence

(1) Preparations for the Eastern Hebei Bank

The Eastern Hebei Bank has been under discussion for a long time. The Japanese side originally planned to make it subordinate to the Bank of Korea, but then thought that the Bank of Korea's access to the economic situation in Hebei and Chahar was not yet possible, so it changed to rely on the Central Bank of Manchuria. They are also preparing for the establishment of a so-called "North China Central Bank," and the function of the Eastern Hebei Bank is a transitional bank in North China. However, at present, its activity ability is only limited to the Eastern Hebei war zone. Its capital is tentatively set at 500,000 yuan. It is said that it will definitely be established within the year.

(2) Kanebo Textile Company's Pulp Factory

"Kanebo" is a famous Japanese textile trust, and the Pulp factory here is directly under the Japanese "Xingzhong Company." Eastern Hebei produces a lot of reeds, and the Eastern Hebei puppet government provides absolute convenience, so they have already established a reed Pulp factory here, which is said to be very successful. In order to complete the consistent artificial silk industry ×× plan, there is also a so-called second decision plan, preparing to add artificial silk and processing factories. Now they have completed the investigation and are actively preparing.

(3) New Factory of Dongya Tobacco Company

Dongya Tobacco Company is also a large-scale Japanese tobacco company. They have decided to open a new factory in Qinhuangdao. The base of this factory has been purchased to 20,000 tsubo (one tsubo is equal to six square feet in our country), and 20 cigarette machines are planned to be installed. The factory will soon be formally established. It is said that the establishment of this factory was entrusted by the Eastern Hebei puppet government. It has obtained the Eastern Hebei tobacco monopoly, which goes without saying.

Now, Japanese small merchants are also paying close attention to the industry and commerce of Eastern Hebei. They have organized a large investigation team to conduct on-site investigations.

Great Shanghai Scenery

Flea Circus and Live Head Chop

— Lang Dejun

A flea, also known as a gnat, is a parasite that is smaller than a grain of rice, and specializes in parasitizing humans, cats, and dogs, and living by sucking blood. It is the most unwelcome thing. But in Shanghai, which has everything, there is a flea circus, which has attracted thousands of people to watch it. At the same time, in that place, there are also live head chops and live people in knife chop boxes and other large sets of magic. This is not surprising to those who have seen it, but if you have not seen it with your own eyes, it is worth talking about, right?

I am a person who wants to see everything new and strange. I can't help but want to see the great skills of the small parasites, so I went to the fourth floor of the Great New Company and spent two dimes on a ticket to visit. Walking inside, I saw a large square table surrounded by people, and the flea circus was starting. The square table was very large, eight feet long and six feet wide. In the center of the table, there was a white board, more than three feet long and about two feet wide. On both sides of this white board, there were many Fujian lacquer boxes inlaid with fish bones, some round, some rectangular, and some square. A flea conductor in his thirties, wearing only a white shirt and Western-style suit, rolled up his sleeves and exposed his wrists, sitting opposite the audience. While taking fleas out of the lacquer boxes to perform, he said to the audience, "The life of a flea is naturally very short, but I can keep it alive for a year. Now, I am offering a reward of 900 yuan. Whoever can keep a flea alive for two months can have this 500 yuan." Someone in the audience said, "It jumps away, where can you find it?" The flea keeper smiled again and said, "Please see! Fleas must be tied up to be raised!" As he spoke, he held a small pliers in his right hand, opened the lid of a lacquer box with his left hand, and clipped out the flea together with the hair-like thread that connected it, and held it up for everyone to see. Afraid that everyone could not see clearly, he also prepared a small microscope, which could actually be called a small magnifying glass, which could be held in the hand to look at. He fastened a flea behind the mirror and handed it to everyone to pass around. Sure enough, a lively flea was swinging there happily, as if waiting. While everyone was passing the flea around, he said to the audience, "Take a look, it's convenient for you, but it's not convenient for me to tie this thread. If it's too tight, the flea will be strangled to death; if it's too loose, it will run away in a while. I am a skilled flea tyer, and it takes me twenty minutes to tie one. Gentlemen, it may take you one or two hours to tie one? If you don't believe me, try it." But no one in the audience answered. After a pause, a spectator asked, "What does the flea eat?" The flea conductor said, "To tell you the truth, it simply eats me. Fleas eat my blood to live; I rely on them to perform to support myself. It eats me, and I eat it, half and half." Before he finished speaking, everyone burst into laughter, and the sound of laughter was endless. Then, without further ado, the flea show began. The flea conductor took out a small copper car from a larger box, but it was only half the size of a small matchbox. A small flea was tied to the shaft of the car, and he shouted "Oh, Go" with his finger pointing. Sure enough, the small flea walked forward step by step, and the car followed. At the same time, he also took out a copper road roller, which also walked like the car. Someone couldn't help but ask him in surprise, "Fleas can only jump, right? No one has ever seen it walk step by step! How do you train it?" The conductor said, "Please take a look!" While speaking, he took out a hanging object from a box that looked a bit like a hand-held incense burner. It was a small copper chain with a flea hanging on it. "Fleas can't be allowed to jump all the time. If they jump all the time, they will jump to their death in the Huangpu River. So I first have to get it used to walking. But how can I make it walk when it can only jump? So I came up with this way of hanging it. The chain is dozens of times heavier than it, so it wants to jump but can't. Also pay attention when hanging it, so that its feet can still touch the ground. Naturally, it will walk. The cars that the fleas dragged just now were each two thousand times heavier than the flea itself. After many tests, we know that fleas have a very strong load-bearing capacity. We have tested it: if we put a ball that is five hundred times heavier than it on its neck, it will carry it without any effort!" As he spoke, he took out a small ball and did the same for the audience to see. After a pause, he announced that he would teach the fleas to kick the ball. First, he took the ball off its neck and placed it on the flea's feet, teaching it to grab it with its feet. He also made a sound to teach it to kick it away. As long as he shouted, "Oh, Go!" The flea would kick the ball one or two feet away. After several tests, it obeyed the command respectfully. At this time, the conductor announced, "Everyone, the minds of each flea are very simple, so each can only do one trick. As soon as it hears my voice, it will do the same, but it is really the same, and it will never come up with new tricks." Then, he took out a small round piano, which looked like a round table. The flat, large tabletop was often used as a dance floor, and the piano underneath could make a dong dong sound. He used small pliers to clip out four or five more fleas, but each of these fleas was covered in a piece of clothing, which was a special conical funnel-shaped clothing. When the little fleas heard the sound of the music, they were just spinning around, like dancing the hula. After that, he took out a roulette frame, which was four inches square. He said, "There is a roulette in the middle that looks like a waterwheel, and its weight is about five thousand times that of a flea. Now, let a flea come to drag it." As he spoke, he took out a flea, placed it under the roulette in a slightly protruding place, and the conductor shouted "Oh, Go" – The following continues on the fifth edition.

sound, and the roulette turned. However, it was turning very weakly. After the roulette was finished, the flea show was over. Because people were crowding in front and behind, I heard someone shouting loudly in another place: "Gentlemen who have finished watching the flea show, please come here to see the live head chop." In this shout, a large group of people rushed to the place where the heads were being chopped like a tide. The setting there was very gloomy and terrible, like a execution ground during the French Revolution. A guillotine stood high, with a large chopper hanging high between two long wooden pillars. The magician who hosted the show even took the time to test the weight of the chopper falling in front of everyone. I saw him flick the button, and quickly with a "clatter" sound, the large knife fell down, shaking the wooden platform for a long time. After a while, a fairly modern young woman appeared before everyone's eyes, with a pointy chin and a very gentle face. After a command from the host, she walked behind the guillotine and put her head into a concave-shaped place to wait for execution. At this time, the host shouted loudly again: "Everyone, look carefully, you may as well stand closer! Watch us chop off this girl's head!" At this time, some timid people left without watching. I knew clearly that it was magic. No matter what trickery it used, it would never really kill anyone. So I squeezed to the front to watch. I saw the host press the same high-hanging chopper button that had been tested, and a large chopper fell suddenly, looking like it was really chopping off the woman's head. However, the woman's face did not change, and she was still as if nothing had happened. After that, the host took out a yellow cloth wrap, shook it open, and put it on the head, saying that he had put the head in here. Sure enough, in the blink of an eye, the head under the chopper disappeared. Because my purpose was to watch the flea show, and it was getting late, and people were squeezing too much, I left before everyone else dispersed. I gave up watching the set of people in the knife chop box.

Book Review

Introducing "The Public Forum"

— Zhao Yi

——Sold by Shanghai Shenzhou Guoguang Press, Price per copy: 1 Jiao——

"The Public Forum" is a recently published comprehensive bi-monthly magazine. Judging from this inaugural issue, its content is indeed relatively complex; it includes explanations of the international situation, research on Chinese issues, short commentaries, specialized treatises, and more. From the viewpoints of the various articles and their specific content, it can be said to be a publication worthy of reading.

The first article, serving as the inaugural address, is "The Recent Ten-Year Evolutionary Trend in the Chinese Publishing Industry" by the journal's editor, Wang Yucun. The author points out that "1926 was a watershed year in modern Chinese history," explaining that the great changes at that time "opened up a new path for the cultural and publishing circles" in China, enabling "China's emerging cultural ideas to establish a dominant position in the cultural and publishing circles." He then divides the changes in the Chinese publishing industry from 1926 to the present into three periods: the first period being the few years around 1926, the second period being around the "September 18th" Incident in 1931, and the present being the third period. He points out that the significant trends in each period are: "The first period mainly involved the translation and introduction of works on general progressive social sciences from around the world; the second period mainly involved the exploration and discussion of the history of Chinese social development; the third period mainly involves the clarification and popularization of the basic knowledge of the above two aspects." Such division and explanation may still require discussion, but at present, raising such questions and the author's expressed opinions are worthy of special attention, although the actual materials in the article are still lacking.

There are four articles explaining the international situation. The first is Qian Yishi's "The Eighteenth Anniversary of the World Armistice Commemoration." Although this is a timely commemorative article, we can see from it the new contradictions that have arisen in the post-war world, as well as the opposing situation between the "aggression front" and the "peace front" in the current international arena; it can be said to be a general and comprehensive analysis of the current international situation. The second is Peng Shumei's "International Struggle Revolving Around the Spanish Question." In this article, the author not only describes the current situation of the Spanish War but also explains the meaning of the non-intervention agreement, and further exposes the "true face of London's attitude towards the Spanish Civil War" from the perspective of Britain's own interests. The other two articles are Ji Zi's "A Perspective on Belgium's Restoration of Neutrality" and Shumei's "The Anti-Soviet Cooperation Between Italy and Germany." The former analyzes the significance and impact of Belgium's restoration of its neutral status from the perspective of its domestic and international situation, while the latter explains the recent plots of Germany and Italy and their threat to world peace.

In this issue of "The Public Forum," the articles that study Chinese issues are most worthy of mentioning. For example, Wang Yucun's "Imperialism and the Construction of China's National Economy" very practically explains, from the current situation of North China's economy, the encounters of China's textile industry, the significance of currency reform, the development of the transportation industry, and the relationship between imperialism and the sales of goods in China, the crisis of relying on the capital of aggressive countries to develop China's industry, breaking the dream of using imperialist capital to peacefully build the national economy. However, according to the author's opinion, one should naturally arrive at the conclusion that it is necessary for the Chinese nation to achieve liberation in order to independently develop our national economy, and that China's current problem is a national problem and a political problem, not a purely economic problem. Unfortunately, the author did not fully and clearly express this point, which can be said to be a slight flaw. Furthermore, Sun Huai-ren's "Soaring Grain Prices in a Year of Great Harvest" also points out, based on the actual situation, the two major reasons for the "soaring grain prices in a year of great harvest": concerns about currency inflation and large-scale absorption by foreign merchants, and explains its dangers. Finally, Gao Su-ming's "The Essence and Activities of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army" not only allows us to know the general struggle of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army but also allows us to understand the recent qualitative changes of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army; all those who care about China's national liberation should read this article.

"On Modern Youth" (Su Dan), which can be regarded as a special treatise, is also a rare essay. It is compiled and translated based on the works of the Japanese author Tosaka Jun, and it makes a profound study and explanation of the characteristics of modern youth and their various aspects. The author says: "With the evolution of the times, modern society is divided into two. The generation of youth in their prime is in one kind of society, and the youth of today are in another kind of society. Times are different, and the conditions of social life are different. In the past, youth only planned to wait for the time to come and smoothly become the successors of those in their prime, but now they are either eager to climb the social ladder of those in their prime due to the shadows of unemployment and poverty, or they harbor dissatisfaction with the established society in which those in their prime are located; these two trends cause sharp antagonism with those in their prime." This is the explanation for the de-youthification of many modern youths, which is the characteristic of the youth in the "era of conflict between father and son." Following this, it also makes a correct explanation of the relationship between modern youth and the general working masses and women, allowing us to know in what way they are similar in terms of being socially oppressed.

Guo Dali's "The Tomorrow of Chinese Culture" is a critique of Zhang Junli's "Theory of Free Culture." The author first explains the essence of Mr. Zhang's "Theory of Free Culture" from a social point of view; then, from the dialectical development of social culture, he criticizes the error of Mr. Zhang's compromising and timid method of establishing a new Chinese culture, saying that "new culture must be the negation of old culture," and that "thorough criticism is the only method for establishing a new culture, and conservatism will inevitably lead to the destruction of culture." These are all very correct views. However, regarding whether it is still possible for China to establish a capitalist culture at a time when the entire capitalism is declining, and regarding whose consciousness Zhang Junli's theory ultimately reflects, the author has not clearly expressed or fully explained, which prevents us from clearly understanding what the author's opinion is.

In addition, this issue of "The Public Forum" also contains short commentaries, domestic and foreign dispatches, literary and artistic treatises, and other writings, all of which are relatively readable.

Speaking of our hopes for the journal, there are also a few points: first, a comprehensive journal should have more complex and rich content so that readers can gain knowledge in many aspects; second, such a journal should have sufficient combativeness, and more polemical articles should be published, otherwise, it will become too mediocre; third, at a time when the problem of national liberation has become the most important problem, it should use great strength to awaken the Chinese people and work hard for the national salvation movement.

A Week of Travel

A Day Trip to Saigon (Conclusion)

— Ms. Ming

We sadly bid farewell to the Dean of Studies and took a tram straight to the zoo. The Saigon Zoo does not require admission tickets; anyone, rich or poor, noble or lowly, can freely enter. This park occupies two to three hundred acres and has all the tropical plants and animals. We left the country after the Mid-Autumn Festival when sweet osmanthus was fragrant, but here we saw lotus flowers in full bloom, admiring their reflections on the water. Unexpectedly, we spent two summers this year—The most numerous animals in the park are monkeys, with no less than eighty or ninety in a cage. This cage has no top, so these "ancestors of mankind" often manage to sneak out and run around the park, snatching food from tourists' hands. Besides monkeys, there are turtles. Speaking of the turtles here, some are as big as myths. Mr. Ye, who was traveling with me, is a bit nearsighted and plump. After walking around the park, he was tired and wanted to find a stone step to sit on. He searched around and saw a yellowish-brown stone block the size of a square table on the grass. He was overjoyed and ran to sit down, but before he reached it, the square table automatically and gracefully walked towards the pool. It turned out to be a large "turtle"—

After enjoying those exotic flowers and rare birds, fierce lions, and trained elephants, we strolled out of the back door of the park. It was about four o'clock in the afternoon, but the sunlight was still very strong. The back of the park was very quiet. Under the shade of those large trees, many Annamese natives were deeply asleep, their sleeping faces showing great comfort and leisure, as if they didn't think about anything other than getting a little comfort at this moment. Not far from the back door of the park, there is a primary school run by a Frenchman, which is exclusively for the children of the Annamese. All expenses are waived, and clothes and hats are also given, so there are many students. We did not go inside to visit, but only stood on the road and looked in through the window, and saw a young Annamese man holding a teaching whip and teaching a class of children about ten years old French. Of course, Annamese was still used for explanation, but the French he recited was truly fluent. When he saw our group staring at him, a proud look appeared on his face, as if saying: "Look, the French also value me——" We had already learned a vague outline of the Annamese youth from a French priest on the same ship. Those who have no money do not go to school and become literate, and work as cattle and horses all day for a living. Those who have money go to French schools, learn excellent French, and then go to France to study, but the French only allow them to study subjects such as chemistry and medicine, and do not allow them to study law, politics, economics, etc. After they complete their studies and return to their country, they are assigned to work as teachers, doctors, or pharmacists, etc.

The ship stopped in Saigon for four days. I only visited here for one day, and my heart was filled with depression. I did not go ashore for the remaining three days. In addition to reading, I stood alone at the bow, looking out at the panoramic view of Saigon—This paradise, known as the "Dreamland" of the East, is no longer a paradise for its native children and its close relatives, the Chinese!

Fragments of Brocade

— Wan Yu

A Latin poet said: "Whoever starts to do something has already succeeded halfway: on the contrary, whoever only does half of it is the same as not doing it at all."

"People should not be arrogant before the final goal is reached: if the goal has been reached, there is no need to be arrogant."

George Bernard Shaw said: "Friends are the best, and can have long-term relationships; parents and siblings are not freely chosen, so they must be left."

An Arab poet said: "Heaven on earth is in the scriptures of the sages, on horseback, and on women's breasts."

Amateur Cafe

Sichuan Cuisine and Sichuan Opera (1)

— Yao Chensha

Speaking of Sichuan cuisine, some people's tongues start to itch. Indeed, one of the main characteristics of Sichuan cuisine is that spicy taste that inexplicably stimulates people's taste organs. If you absolutely prohibit Sichuan chefs from using spicy flavors, no matter how skilled they are, many dishes cannot be made well. As for Sichuan opera, it has only recently been moved out from the distant thousands of miles away, from inside the [unclear] gate; its main characteristic, apart from the aspects of theatrical performance, is the use of gongs and drums, which are especially noisy and shocking to people's eardrums when they are played, and can also be said to be very stimulating. If it is said that Sichuan people's temperament is active rather than quiet, strong rather than gentle, and combative rather than willing to be humiliated, then in terms of Sichuan cuisine and Sichuan opera, we can probably get some explanation for the character of Sichuan people.

Judging from the recent situation, Sichuan cuisine seems to be developing more and more. Look, isn't the originally very quiet Huagene Road very lively now? When you walk along this road at lunchtime or dinnertime, you can see nearly ten consecutive Sichuan restaurants, all with many people eating or feasting there. Although we still don't know the actual business situation of those restaurants, it is quite remarkable that so many restaurants of the same nature have appeared in one place within a short period of time, and that so many people actually go to patronize them. As for Sichuan opera? We know that it once opened at the Xinguang Grand Theatre, but it soon stopped: now it has come back again, performing upstairs in the Dahua Ballroom, and it is said that it can still sell tickets, but no matter what, compared to the development of Sichuan cuisine, it is somewhat inferior. What is the reason for this? Everyone who knows Sichuan cuisine and Sichuan opera will have this question. I think the first thing to pay attention to is the so-called "stimulation" problem.
